601 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fullwood


No. 124, April Term, 1968


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


214 Pa. Super. 135; 251 A.2d 677; 1969 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1383


November 11, 1968, Argued  
March 20, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of sentence of Criminal Court of Fayette County, No. 474 of 1966, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Etta Fullwood.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence reversed and case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of sentence entered by the Criminal Court of Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's motions in arrest of judgment and for a new trial and convicted appellant of embezzlement by a public officer, in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4822, and fraudulent conversion of property, in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4834.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's convictions resulted from a shortage in the accounts at the county treasurer's office where she worked. The commonwealth presented evidence that appellant retained daily deposits and did not deposit funds. Appellant contended that the fraudulent conversion of property charge under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4834 was unfounded because the county was not a "person" within the meaning of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4103, but the court held that political subdivisions were included within the definition of "person." Appellant also contended that the embezzlement by a public officer charge was unfounded because she was not a public officer, but the court held that 18 Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4822 applied to any officer, employee, or agent of a political subdivision that exercised any control over public funds. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in denying her motion in arrest of judgment because the evidence was insufficient to show misapplication and because there was no demand made upon her to return the money. The court found that the circumstantial evidence amply supported that appellant withheld funds, altered deposit records, and reported a false robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for embezzlement by a public officer and fraudulent conversion of property because the commonwealth's evidence clearly established that appellant exercised improper control over public funds. However, the court reversed for resentencing because appellant was sentenced for an indefinite term at the state correctional institution under the Muncy Act, which was held to be unconstitutional.

603 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


First Trinity Evangelical Lutheran Church Appeal


No. 109, April Term, 1968


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


214 Pa. Super. 185; 251 A.2d 685; 1969 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1391


November 11, 1968, Argued  
March 20, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Allegheny County, June T., 1967, No. 161, in re petition of First Trinity Evangelical Lutheran Church in the City of Pittsburgh.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner church sought review of an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied its request for authority to abandon a cemetery, re-inter the remains at another cemetery, and sell the property.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner church applied to the trial court for authority to abandon its cemetery, re-inter the remains of the people buried there, and sell the land. Family members of those interred answered the petition. The trial court denied the petition, holding that the site could not be abandoned under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 9, § 48.1 (1959). The cemetery site was remote when purchased, but in the hundred years since that time became surrounded by housing projects and a university. The cemetery was not well maintained and the city had closed most of the roads providing access to the cemetery. The court rejected the claim of one plot owner that he owned his plot in fee simple. The court found that the cemetery had become angular and partly surrounded by improvements and could therefore be abandoned under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 9, § 48.1(1) (1959). The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of petitioner church's request for authority to abandon its cemetery because the cemetery was statutorily eligible for abandonment.

606 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Galloway


No. 1130, October Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


212 Pa. Super. 154; 239 A.2d 893; 1968 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1083


December 11, 1967, Submitted  
March 21, 1968, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County, March T., 1964, No. 69, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Kenneth Augustus Galloway.



DISPOSITION: Record remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal sought review of an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of sodomy and solicitation to commit sodomy and sentenced him to serve a term of not less than two and one-half nor more than five years.


OVERVIEW: After appellant criminal was convicted of sodomy and solicitation to commit sodomy, appellant petitioned the lower court for relief under the Post Conviction Hearing Act (Act), 19 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1180-1 et seq. (Supp. 1966). Although the lower court appointed counsel to represent appellant, it dismissed appellant's petition without a hearing. Appellant contended that the lower court erred in dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief without having allowed counsel an opportunity to present written or oral argument in support of the petition. In disagreeing, the court stated that the Act's language did not mandate that counsel be given the opportunity to appear before the lower court to explain why an evidentiary hearing was warranted. The court did, however, remand the case for an evidentiary hearing because the lower court erred in dismissing appellant's allegations that evidence obtained pursuant to an unlawful arrest and search and seizure was used to procure his conviction. The court noted that the Act specifically provided that appellant could have raised these allegations in a post-conviction petition subsequent to his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the lower court's order denying appellant criminal's petition for post-conviction relief because appellant should have been allowed to raise allegations that commonwealth used unlawfully obtained evidence to secure his convictions. The Post Conviction Hearing Act, however, did not require the lower court to allow defense counsel an opportunity to present argument in support of the petition.

 

607 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Ulmer


No. 295, October Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


211 Pa. Super. 193; 238 A.2d 38; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 751


June 12, 1967, Submitted  
November 16, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County, Dec. T., 1958, No. 141, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Lloyd Ulmer.



DISPOSITION: Ordered that petitioner be credited with time served under invalid sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate pleaded guilty to aggravated assault and battery and was sentenced in July 1959 to a term of one and one-half to three years. He eventually was granted a new trial before the Court of Quarter Sessions of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania) where he was found guilty of assault and battery. The inmate appealed the order by which he was sentenced to one year's imprisonment, to begin at the expiration of his 1961 sentences.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was released on parole in January 1961. He was again arrested on charges of assault and battery and was sentenced in June 1961 to a term of three to six years. This sentence was to begin after the completion of the one and one-half years remaining on his earlier sentence. In September 1961, he was convicted of a prison breach and was sentenced to one and one-half to three years, to begin at the expiration of the sentence imposed in June 1961. His petition for a writ of habeas corpus was granted in 1964, and the record was remanded for the new trial on the 1959 charge. In his petition before the court, he contended that he had to be given credit for the time served under the invalid 1959 sentence. The court held that because the inmate had been retried for the same acts, credits should be awarded. The Act of August 14, 1963, § 1, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 898, required that a defendant convicted after a new trial had to receive credit for time served under an invalid sentence for the same criminal acts. The maximum sentence for assault and battery was two years. As a result of the proceedings, the inmate could have served up to two and one-half years for that offense.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the inmate be credited with time served under the invalid sentence.

 

608 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Caddie Homes, Inc. v. Falic


No. 795, October Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


211 Pa. Super. 333; 235 A.2d 437; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 781


September 14, 1967, Argued  
November 16, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Refused December 12, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1965, No. 2372, in case of Caddie Homes, Inc. et al. v. Fima Falic et al.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the insurer's objections to jurisdiction in appellee employer's action in foreign attachment.


OVERVIEW: The employer, a Maryland subsidiary of a Pennsylvania corporation, advanced money to the employee, a resident of Maryland, to assist him after he was injured in an automobile accident. Despite a written agreement to repay the money, the employee refused to return the money after the insurer began making workers' compensation payments. The employer instituted an action in foreign attachment in Pennsylvania, summoning the insurer as garnishee. The insurer continued to make payments to the employee and filed objections to jurisdiction, which were dismissed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court was not required to adhere to Maryland laws that exempted such funds from attachment. The laws of attachment were governed by the law of the forum, not the law of the state where the debt arose. There was no constitutional compulsion to grant full faith and credit to exemptions created under the Maryland statute, nor was the attachment contrary to Pennsylvania's public policy. The possibility that the employee's right to receive future weekly payments could be modified through the settlement of his claim against a third party did not affect the unconditional nature of the weekly payments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the insurer's objections to jurisdiction in the employer's action in foreign attachment.

 

609 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Primoli v. Philadelphia Bronze & Brass Corp.


No. 15, October Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


211 Pa. Super. 224; 238 A.2d 29; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 756


March 23, 1967, Argued  
November 16, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1966, No. 324, in case of Sante Primoli v. Philadelphia Bronze & Brass Corporation et al.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and an insurer, challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that reinstated a referee's award to appellee employee after the award was reversed by the Workmen's Compensation Board.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained an eye injury while working for the employer. He received workmen's compensation for total disability over the course of several months, pursuant to a compensation agreement. A final receipt was executed after his disability terminated. Sixteen years later, the employee applied for reinstatement of compensation under the Workmen's Compensation Act, § 413, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 77, § 772 (Supp.). The referee granted compensation, however, the Board reversed the referee's ruling. The court adopted the referee's ruling, finding that the claim was not time-barred. Although the statute of limitations applicable at the time of the original injury would have precluded the claim, the court held that the "unlimited" maximum benefit period "statute of limitations" in effect at the filing of the reinstatement petition, Act of February 28, 1956, P.L. 1120 (1955), was applicable. The Act was deemed to be procedural and therefore applicable to the employee's proceeding before the referee even though the petition involved an accident that occurred before its enactment. The law in effect on the date that the petition for reinstatement controlled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

610 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Williams


Nos. 157, 164, October Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


210 Pa. Super. 388; 234 A.2d 37; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1012


March 27, 1967, Argued  
September 15, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from orders of County Court of Philadelphia, Nos. 135483 and 136162, in the matters of John Williams and Ardry Jones.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juveniles challenged the decision of the County Court of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), which entered separate orders committing the juveniles as defective delinquent juveniles to the State Correctional Institution.


OVERVIEW: The juveniles contended that the trial court was without power to order their confinement at the location ordered because the legislature designated the authority to transfer to and from the location to have been placed with the Department of Justice. The court rejected this contention, holding that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 542.3 placed the administrative authority of the institutions under control of the Department of Justice in the Deputy Commissioner for Treatment of the Bureau of Correction, and had not taken any power of sentencing and commitment from the courts. The determination of the question of whether one was mentally defective and had criminal tendencies and as to where he should have been committed was vested in the courts under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 541-3. Although the proceedings began by a petition for discharge of the juveniles from another institution, it culminated in an original proceeding as to acts committed while the juveniles were in custody, a determination of delinquency, that they were mentally defective with criminal tendencies, and a commitment as a result of these findings. This was not a transfer but an original act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

611 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Leonardziak Liquor License Case


No. 292, October Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


210 Pa. Super. 511; 233 A.2d 606; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1034


June 19, 1967, Argued  
September 15, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Berks County, No. 7455 Miscellaneous Docket, 1966, in re suspension of restaurant liquor license No. R-2849 issued to William P. Leonardziak.



DISPOSITION: Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Liquor Control Board challenged an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Berks County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the challenge of appellee licensee to a fine against him.


OVERVIEW: The Liquor Control Board fined the licensee for having maintained gambling devices and paraphernalia on the licensed premises. At a hearing de novo, the trial court excluded the Board's only evidence as having been unlawfully obtained and sustained licensee's appeal. The Board appealed conceding that the evidence in question was acquired by police detectives pursuant to an invalid search warrant and could not be used in a court of law, but arguing that the evidence could be considered at a Board citation hearing. The Board argued that holding a license was a privilege, and thus, due process did not require that the evidence obtained through an invalid warrant be excluded from the Board's consideration. The court found, however, that the Board was empowered to impose a fine that was equal to or greater than that which could be imposed under the criminal law. Thus, evidence that could not be used in a court of law could not be used to impose a penalty of equal or greater severity by the Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order.

 

612 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Bessemer & L. E. R. Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


Nos. 133, 134, 135, 136, 137, 138, 139, 140, 141, 142, 143, 144, March Term, 1966, 108, 109, 110, April Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


210 Pa. Super. 7; 232 A.2d 220; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 948


March 14, 1967, Argued  
June 16, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from orders of Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission at Petition Docket No. 7, and Complaint Docket C. 18018 for appeal No. 142, in case of Bessemer and Lake Erie Railroad Company et al. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroads appealed from two orders of appellee Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission ordering the railroads to promulgate appropriate operating rules to provide flagging protection when a train stopped or was moving under circumstances in which it might be overtaken by another train.


OVERVIEW: The railroads contended that the flagging protection sought to be achieved by the Commission was no longer necessary under automatic block and similar signal systems and that the orders were not the result of any procedure authorized by law. In affirming, the court found that the orders were within the powers of the Commission as authorized by the Public Utility Law and that in substance, the proceedings were complaints against the carriers with regard to their failure to observe ostensibly necessary flagging requirements Further, the court found that the Commission was granted the power under the Public Utility Law to grant relief to railroad employees whose personal safety was at risk due to working conditions and concluded that the Commission's findings as to the need for flagging protection was supported by substantial competent evidence. The fact that the Interstate Commerce Commission had no outstanding rules concerning flagging meant that the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania had the power to take care of such a needed protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the commission.

 

613 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Daniels


No. 600, October Term, 1966


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


210 Pa. Super. 156; 232 A.2d 247; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 979


December 16, 1966, Argued  
June 16, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, 1966 Session, No. 2280, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Jane M. Daniels.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a woman convicted of robbery, appealed the judgment of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), sentencing her to an indeterminate term of incarceration pursuant to the Muncy Act, 61 P.S. § 566.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a woman, was initially sentenced to one to four years imprisonment after being found guilty of robbery. Thirty one days later, the trial court vacated the first sentence and sentenced defendant to an indeterminate term as required by the Muncy Act (Act). The practical effect to defendant was that the Act caused her to have been given a significantly harsher sentence, solely because she was a woman, than a male defendant would likely have received under similar circumstances. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the Act did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution because the legislature rationally based the Act on its conclusion that, notwithstanding the disparate effect upon women as compared to men, indeterminate sentences needed to be imposed on women as a class, allowing the time of incarceration to be matched to the necessary treatment in order to provide more effective rehabilitation., and that accordingly, the trial court's judgment of sentence was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sentencing defendant to an indeterminate term of incarceration in accordance with the Act.

 

614 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Dooley


No. 102, April Term, 1967


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


209 Pa. Super. 519; 232 A.2d 45; 1967 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1263


April 10, 1967, Argued  
June 16, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Crawford County, Nov. T., 1964, No. 21, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. John Dooley, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Crawford County (Pennsylvania), reinstating an original sentence which it had vacated on constitutionality grounds and holding that the Barr-Walker Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1166-1174, was constitutional and the indeterminate sentence imposed of one day to life met due process requirements thereunder.


OVERVIEW: Pleading guilty to a charge of assault with intent to ravish, defendant was sentenced to a term of one day to life under the Barr-Walker Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, §§ 1166-1174 and not under the provisions of the Penal Code, June 24, 1939, P.L. 872, § 722, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit.18, § 4722, based on a psychiatric determination that he was a danger as a result of his direct sexual aggressive behavior. After the sentence was vacated, a new hearing was held in which the assistant superintendent of a state hospital testified that the original report was prepared by other doctors under his supervision and that he also had some personal contact with defendant during the course of the examination. The doctor also reiterated his finding that defendant was not mentally ill but did present a danger to society. In reluctantly vacating the sentence and finding the Act unconstitutional, the court held that indeterminate treatment sentencing was a separate criminal proceeding and required a full judicial hearing with all due process procedural safeguards, including counsel, an opportunity to be heard and to confront witnesses, a right to cross-examination, and for defendant to offer evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cause for sentencing in accord with the penal statutes.

 

615 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Vecchiolli


Nos. 566, 606, October Term, 1966


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


208 Pa. Super. 483; 224 A.2d 96; 1966 Pa. Super. LEXIS 873


September 16, 1966, Argued  
November 17, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of Court of Quarter Sessions of Carbon County, June T., 1965, No. 26, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Frank Vecchiolli, alias Frank Rossatti, et al.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments entered in the Court of Quarter Sessions of Carbon County (Pennsylvania) that denied their motion for a new trial following their conviction of the crime of assault with intent to rob.


OVERVIEW: Following their convictions for assault with intent to rob, defendants appealed and presented several challenges to the validity of their convictions. First, defendants argued that error occurred because they were not given a sufficient number of challenges as to the jury venire. The court rejected this argument and noted that jointly indicted defendants received the same number of total challenges as a single defendant. Second, defendants argued that error occurred when the trial court refused to allow them to call an alibi witness. The court rejected this argument and found that defendants were not entitled to call an alibi witness because they had failed to provide prior notice of this witness to the prosecutor. Further, the law that required defendants to give prior notice of alibi witnesses was constitutional. Third, the court found that the refusal of the trial court to sequester the Commonwealth's witnesses and to confine the jury was not error, as defendants failed to show any prejudice resulting from the trial court's actions here. Finally, no error occurred when a prosecution witness gave the name of her accomplice to a crime she was serving at the time she testified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of sentence imposed by the trial court.

 

616 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Crumlish


Nos. 327, 328, October Term, 1965


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


207 Pa. Super. 516; 218 A.2d 596; 1966 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1153


June 14, 1965, Argued  
April 14, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, Feb. T., 1965, Nos. 266 and 297, in cases of Joseph Smith and William Mullan v. James C. Crumlish, District Attorney for City of Philadelphia.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed a judgment from the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which quashed the indictments of defendants for displaying obscenity, holding that §§ 528 and 529 of the Pennsylvania Penal Code, the Act of June 24, 1939, P.L. 872, Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 4528, 4529, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county detective applied to a magistrate for a search and seizure warrant that asserted that a motion picture displayed by defendants in two theaters was obscene. After the magistrate issued the warrant, the motion picture was seized and defendants were indicted for obscenity. Defendants filed motions to quash the indictments and to suppress the evidence. The trial court quashed the indictments because it concluded that both §§ 528 and 529 of the Pennsylvania Penal Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, §§ 4528, 4529, were unconstitutional. The Commonwealth asserted that the statutory provisions that barred the exhibition of the motion pictures or the display of advertisements for the motion pictures were vague and overbroad. On appeal, the court reviewed the law and concluded that the trial court erred when it found that § 4528 was unconstitutionally vague; however, the court held that the terms "indecent" and "immoral" used in § 4529 to described materials that were prohibited were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

617 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. County of Allegheny v. Shenot


No. 166, April Term, 1965


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


207 Pa. Super. 351; 218 A.2d 76; 1966 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1121


November 8, 1965, Argued  
March 24, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of County Court of Allegheny County, No. C 1474 of 1964, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. County of Allegheny v. J. W. Shenot.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a farm operator, sought review of an order from the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of violating county health department rules by selling unpasteurized milk for human consumption without a permit.


OVERVIEW: The court initially held that the county health department had the authority to enact regulations governing milk and milk products because the state Milk Control Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 700j-101 et seq., did not preclude local authorities from promulgating milk regulations that were at least as strict as the state regulations. However, the court found Allegheny County, Pa., Health Department Rules and Regulations 505 to be an invalid exercise of the county's police power because it prohibited the sale in the county of any milk that was not pasteurized. The assumption that unpasteurized milk could not be made safe for human consumption was inconsistent with the state legislature's regulations governing categories of milk. While the court found that the permit requirement of Allegheny County, Pa., Health Department Rules and Regulations 504(A) was not unconstitutional per se, defendant was entitled to a permit because the testimony showed that the only reason defendant was denied a permit was because the health department issued no permits for raw milk. Such a criterion was, in itself, insufficient to deny a permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order convicting defendant and ordered defendant discharged.

 

618 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Kaminsky


No. 505, October Term, 1965


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


206 Pa. Super. 480; 214 A.2d 251; 1965 Pa. Super. LEXIS 833


September 13, 1965, Argued  
November 10, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, May T., 1965, No. 961 Miscellaneous Docket, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Sherman C. Kaminsky, also known as Paul A. Vargo.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was paroled from a New York prison and permitted by lawful agreement to reside in Maryland. In the agreement, he waived extradition to New York for any parole violation. Defendant appealed an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which remanded him to the New York authorities based on the procedures provided in the Compact Act of June 25, 1937, P.L. 2086, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, §§ 321, 322.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had violated his New York parole by leaving Maryland and entering Pennsylvania. After his arrest in Pennsylvania, the lower court held that defendant was not entitled to extradition proceedings and ordered that defendant be delivered to New York. On appeal, defendant contended that the lower court erred in following the Compact Act and that it should have applied the provisions of the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act of July 8, 1941, P.L. 288, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19 § 191.1 et seq. The court disagreed with defendant's contention and upheld the lower court's order. The New York parole agreement that permitted defendant to reside in Maryland specifically stated that defendant would not contest any effort to return him to New York.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order. Defendant was directed to appear in the lower court at such time as he may there be called to comply with the terms of such order.

Harry C. Erb, Inc. v. Shell Constr. Co.

620 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Lima Bldg. Stone Quarry, Inc. v. Commonwealth


No. 683, October Term, 1964


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


205 Pa. Super. 365; 208 A.2d 884; 1965 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1080


March 16, 1965, Argued  
April 15, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, No. 3517 of 1964, in case of Lima Building Stone Quarry, Inc. v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Highways.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which quashed his appeal of a decision from a quarter sessions court assessing damages for the taking of his land by appellee Commonwealth because it was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The owner contended that the 30-day provision of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 36, § 670-303 (1945) did not apply. Under the Act of 1945, an appeal had to be filed within 30 days after the filing of the report. The court rejected the contention that it only applied when the parties waived the waiting period. The filing of exceptions to a viewer's report was independent of the right to take an appeal from the report, and there was no inconsistency in filing exceptions and in entering an appeal at the same time. The owner further contended that the Act of 1945, as interpreted, was unconstitutional as violative of Pa. Const. art. 3, § 3, in that the subject matter of appeals from the report of viewers was not mentioned in the title of the act. The Act of 1945 was a complete embodiment of the law insofar as state highways are concerned. It was not necessary to mention every provision of the bill in the title. Because the appeal from the viewers' report was filed beyond the time provided by the Act of 1945, it was properly quashed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

621 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Ullman


No. 328, Oct. T., 1964


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


204 Pa. Super. 145; 203 A.2d 386; 1964 Pa. Super. LEXIS 557


June 11, 1964, Argued  
September 17, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, No. 9948 of 1963, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Roland G. E. Ullman, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which granted a supersedeas, allowed defendant's appeal, and reversed an order of a secretary of revenue. The secretary of revenue had informed defendant that his operator's license was revoked following his conviction by a trial court for operating a motor vehicle under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: The secretary of revenue received the pertinent information on a form furnished by a department, signed, and dated by a deputy clerk of courts. There was no possible reason for the court of common pleas to have sustained defendant's appeal even if the court of the common pleas had jurisdiction, which it did not. Defendant never questioned his conviction. Admitting his conviction, he had no standing to question the mere ministerial act of the secretary of revenue in revoking his operator's license as Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 75, § 616 required. The court of common pleas improperly concluded that a person who had his license revoked for one year was deprived of the privilege of applying for a license during that period. Therefore, the person was entitled to appeal from the order of revocation. The court held that an operator's privilege could not be revoked for one year if he could obtain a new license within that period. The privilege, not a card that the person carried in his pocket, was revoked.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the court of common pleas. The court reinstated the revocation of defendant's operator's license. The court ordered defendant to surrender his operator's license to the department.

 

622 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Garner


Nos. 325 and 326, Oct. T., 1964


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


204 Pa. Super. 227; 203 A.2d 333; 1964 Pa. Super. LEXIS 573


June 10, 1964, Argued  
September 17, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, May T., 1944, Nos. 887 and 888, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Eugene Garner, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania appealed a decision of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that set aside a judgment of sentence against defendant and granted a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Without the assistance of counsel, defendant pled guilty to assault and attempted robbery. After he served three years, he was paroled. He was then discharged from parole. He filed a petition to set aside the conviction on the ground that he had not intelligently waived his right to counsel, he was coerced into confessing, and he was drugged at the time of the incident. The petition was brought forth in order to enable him to reduce a sentence imposed on him as a second felony offender in New York. After various appeals and remands, the petition was granted. In reversing the order, the court found that the trial court did not have jurisdiction over defendant or over his judgment of sentence when it granted the petition. There was no jurisdiction because such jurisdiction terminated when defendant was discharged from parole. Since defendant's sentence was fully executed, the power of the trial court to modify or amend the sentence or to impose a new sentence was gone, whether or not the term had expired. The trial court could not proceed to adjudication when there was no subject matter on which the judgment could operate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and dismissed defendant's petition to vacate the judgment of sentence.

 

623 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Gerchman v. Maroney


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


203 Pa. Super. 293; 201 A.2d 319; 1964 Pa. Super. LEXIS 847


Argued April 14, 1964  
June 11, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 101 and 102, April T., 1964, from orders of Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County, Dec. T., 1963, Nos. 264 and 265, in cases of Commonwealth ex rel. Carl G. Gerchman v. James F. Maroney, Superintendent; and Commonwealth ex rel. Delmas Breman McFadden v. Same. Orders affirmed.

Proceedings upon petitions for writs of habeas corpus. Before SOHN, P.J.

Orders entered dismissing petitions. Relators appealed.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeals in two habeas corpus proceedings attacked the constitutionality of the Barr-Walker Act, January 8, 1952, P.L. 1851, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1166, which provided alternative sentencing for sex offenders. One defendant was pleaded guilty to assault with intent to ravish; the other defendant was convicted by a jury of sodomy and solicitation to commit sodomy. Neither defendant was a first offender.


OVERVIEW: The Barr-Walker Act, January 8, 1952, P.L. 1851, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1166 created an alternative sentencing procedure for sex offenders by assigning psychiatrists to examine them, by allowing them to be confined to a mental institution for an indeterminate period of between one day and the rest of their lives, and by requiring periodic review by the Pennsylvania Department of Welfare and the Pennsylvania Board of Parole to determine whether parole was appropriate. In their petitions, defendants argued that the Act violated the due process provisions of the 14th Amendment and the title provisions of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3. The court explained that the Act neither created nor described a crime but merely provided alternative sentencing for someone who had been convicted, with all of the elements of due process, of a crime. The Act was neither cruel and unusual nor vague and indefinite: its procedural provisions were clear. Nor did it punish a condition; instead, the Act sought to rehabilitate and treat habitual sex offenders while protecting the public from them. That the title did not enumerate the applicable sex crimes did not invalidate the Act.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the constitutionality of the Act and affirmed the orders of the court of common pleas.

 

624 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Howe v. Smith


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


203 Pa. Super. 212; 199 A.2d 521; 1964 Pa. Super. LEXIS 835


Argued March 10, 1964  
April 14, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 60, March T., 1964, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Equity No. 2559, No. 544 Commonwealth Docket, 1962, in case of Dr. Joseph W. Howe et al. v. Theodore B. Smith, Jr. et al. Order affirmed.

Equity.

Order entered sustaining defendants' preliminary objections and dismissing complaint, opinion by SOHN, P.J. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractors sought review of the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) that dismissed their amended complaint in equity to enjoin defendant, Secretary of Revenue from refusing to accept certificates from chiropractors concerning the physical fitness of certain motor vehicle operators.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractors did not question the validity of the secretary's authority to require physical and mental examinations of licensees or applicants for licenses for certain motor vehicle operators. However, they contended that by limiting the examinations to physicians and refusing to accept the certificates of chiropractors, the secretary was discriminating against them in violation of the Equal Protection Clauses of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that nothing could be gained by the chiropractors were they given a court hearing or further allowed to amend their complaint. The court ruled that the secretary was not only authorized but was required to reject all certificates of examination made by chiropractors. The court found that the secretary in accepting only examinations certified by physicians was recognizing a real distinction between physicians and chiropractors given him by the legislature to have the examination made by such agencies as the secretary directed. The court ruled that the classification made by the legislature was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the amended complaint filed by the chiropractors.

 

625 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Giaccio


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


202 Pa. Super. 294; 196 A.2d 189; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 563


Argued September 10, 1963  
December 12, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 123, Oct. T., 1963, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Chester County, Sept. T., 1961, No. 225, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Jay Giaccio. Order reversed.

Indictment charging defendant with unlawfully and wantonly pointing and discharging a firearm. Before GAWTHROP, P.J.

Verdict of not guilty; order entered directing defendant to pay costs of prosecution; upon petition for rehearing order entered vacating imposition of costs. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, sentence reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania appealed an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which vacated a sentence imposed by the jury upon defendant to pay the costs of a criminal prosecution after it acquitted him of wantonly pointing and discharging a firearm in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4716.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fired a gun in the air. The Commonwealth charged defendant. Defendant claimed he had shot a blank from a starting pistol. The jury acquitted defendant, but ordered him to pay the costs of the prosecution as provided by Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1222. Defendant moved to set aside the sentence on the basis that § 1222 violated U.S. Const. amend XIV. The trial court set aside the sentence. The Commonwealth appealed. The court reversed and reinstated the sentence. Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1222 or a similar provision had been in force since the earliest days of the Commonwealth. While other state constitutions prohibited the practice, there was no prohibition in the Pennsylvania Constitution. The constitutionality of § 1222 had been upheld after the adoption of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and that precedent was binding. The claim that the provision was inserted in error was refuted by subsequent re-enactment. There was no unlawful delegation of legislative power. The classification of crimes into misdemeanors and felonies was not unconstitutional. The imposition of costs was not punishment for an undefined crime but a recognition that defendant was responsible for the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which had set aside the sentence that required defendant to pay the costs of the prosecution. The court reinstated the sentence.

Commonwealth v. Joyce


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


202 Pa. Super. 350; 197 A.2d 226; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 574


Argued September 11, 1963  
December 12, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 46, March T., 1963, from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of York County, Jan. T., 1961, No. 109, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. David Joyce. Judgment affirmed.

Indictment charging defendant with wilfully possessing and maintaining certain gambling devices. Before ATKINS, P.J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence entered thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, and it is ordered that appellant appear in the court below at such time as he may be there called, and that he be by that court committed until he has complied with his sentence or any part thereof which had not been performed at the time the order of supersedeas was entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Quarter Sessions of York County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of wilfully possessing and maintaining certain gambling devices under § 603 of the Penal Code, the Act of June 24, 1939, P.L, 872, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4603.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of wilfully possessing and maintaining certain gambling devices under § 603 of the Penal Code, the Act of June 24, 1939, P.L. 872, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4603. On appeal, defendant complained that the trial court erred in rejecting certain documentary evidence and depositions to establish his defense that the machines had been purchased for resale to customers in England, and that conversion of the machines to free play devices for foreign shipment was protected by the federal Constitution, and by § 2 of the Johnson Act of January 2, 1951, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1172. The court held that even though the machines may have been intended for interstate commerce, they were not beyond the operation of the penal laws of the Commonwealth. A police statute was not unconstitutional merely because it indirectly involved or burdened interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of wilfully possessing and maintaining certain gambling devices.

In re Auditor's Report for Franklin


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


202 Pa. Super. 415; 200 A.2d 905; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 589


Argued November 14, 1963  
December 12, 1963

Order modified and, as modified, affirmed; that part of order pertaining to costs opened for reargument, by order dated January 29, 1964.

Appeal by township supervisors from report of auditors imposing surcharges.

Order entered sustaining appeal and setting aside surcharge, opinion by VAN DER VOORT, J. Auditor appealed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant auditor sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the appeal of appellee township supervisors, and set aside a surcharge that was imposed upon the township supervisors.


OVERVIEW: A decree to create a borough out of a township was signed and recorded. The elected auditors surcharged the township supervisors for the overpayment of compensation to themselves and for the treasurer's salary. Otherwise, the court affirmed judgment and held that common pleas court was proper in holding the treasurer as a de facto officer. The court opined that the borough received valuable services from the treasurer, and under the circumstances, was required to pay for the services. The court opined that the township supervisors were public officials that were elected to township offices under a law that fixed their maximum compensation. The court concluded that they had no authority to pass legislation that set their salaries in excess of that amount.


OUTCOME: The court modified the common pleas court's order by reinstating the auditor's surcharge of the township supervisors for the excess compensation they paid themselves. Otherwise, the order was affirmed.

Housing Authority of Pittsburgh v. Turner


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


201 Pa. Super. 62; 191 A.2d 869; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 370


Argued April 18, 1963.  
June 12, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 131, April T., 1963, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Excution No. 427, July T., 1962, sur July T., 1962, No. 1701, in case of Housing Authority of City of Pittsburgh v. Genevieve Turner. Order affirmed.

Petition of defendant and rule to show cause why judgment entered by confession on a written lease should not be opened.

Order entered discharging rule, opinion by WEIR, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenant petitioned the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) to rule and show cause why judgment in favor of appellee landlord entered by confession on a written lease should not be opened. The court discharged the rule. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenant's landlord was the Housing Authority of the City of Pittsburgh. The lease was from month to month and authorized either party to terminate the lease on 15 days notice to the other party. The landlord gave the requisite 15 days notice and extended the period for more than a year before bringing its ejectment action. The tenant alleged that permitting the landlord to eject her without just cause was contrary to public policy and deprived her of her rights without due process of law. The court concluded that the landlord was entitled to judgment in ejectment and that the tenant had not been denied due process or deprived of any constitutional right. Although the landlord was a public entity, it had the same right to contract as individuals and the same right to eject a tenant pursuant to a lease provision as did individuals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that dismissed the tenant's petition for rule to show cause why judgment in favor of the landlord entered by confession on a written lease should not be opened.

In re Solomon Liquor License Case


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


201 Pa. Super. 82; 191 A.2d 681; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 375


Argued April 18, 1963.  
June 12, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 129, April T., 1963, from order of County Court of Allegheny County, No. C-2137 of 1962, in re appeal from refusal of application for transfer of restaurant liquor license to Joseph Solomon, trading as Villa Roma. Order reversed.

Appeal by applicant from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board refusing application for transfer of restaurant liquor license.

Order entered sustaining appeal and directing Liquor Control Board to transfer license, opinion by GUFFEY, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board sought review of a decision of the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained an appeal by appellee applicant after the Board refused to transfer a restaurant liquor license and which directed the Board to transfer the license.


OVERVIEW: A building that had a restaurant liquor license was destroyed by fire, and a new building was erected. The applicant sought to transfer another restaurant liquor license to the new building, but the Board refused on the ground that the establishment was within 200 feet of six other licensed establishments. The applicant sought judicial review. The trial court sustained the appeal and directed the Board to transfer the license, finding that the discretion had to be based on facts other than mere distance. The Board appealed. The court reversed, holding that the fact that the location proposed to be licensed was within 200 feet of another licensed establishment was a sufficient basis for the Board's refusal to grant or transfer the license. The restrictive provisions of § 404 of The Pennsylvania Liquor Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-404, as amended by the Act of August 25, 1959, P.L. 746, provided that the Board could refuse a new license or transfer a license for a place within 200 feet of any other licensed premises, and it had to be liberally construed. The trial court had no right to substitute its discretion for that of the Board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision.

School Dist. v. Cambria County Legion Recreation Asso.


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


201 Pa. Super. 163; 192 A.2d 149; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 393


Argued April 15, 1963.  
June 12, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 5, April T., 1963, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Combria County, Sept. T., 1960, No. 1100, in case of School District of Cambria Township v. Cambria County Legion Recreation Association. Order affirmed.

Mandamus upon case stated.

Order entered for plaintiff, opinion by WOLFE, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district sought a writ of mandamus to compel defendant recreation association to charge and collect a tax on charges to the general public for admission to the fairgrounds. The Court of Common Pleas of Combria County (Pennsylvania) upheld the validity of the tax and issued the writ of mandamus. The association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association argued that the school district could only tax admissions to amusements and that the fair was an agricultural and horticultural as well as an industrial exhibition that was not an amusement. Therefore a tax on admissions to its fairgrounds was invalid. The lower court issued a writ of mandamus ordering the association to collect the tax. The court held that the broad language of the taxing part of the school district's resolution included a variety of activities that were not necessarily amusements and specifically included admissions to fairgrounds. Although the fair included agricultural and horticultural exhibits, the fair also included a midway with rides, games, and concession stands that were not directly related to agricultural or horticultural exhibits. The fair charged a general admission fee to the public. The court held that the taxing ordinance was a valid exercise of the school district's taxing authority and that the fairgrounds was required to pay the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Mt. Lebanon v. Hobbes


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


201 Pa. Super. 30; 189 A.2d 316; 1963 Pa. Super. LEXIS 366

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 240, April T., 1962, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, July T., 1959, No. 2996, in case of Township of Mount Lebanon v. Dorrance F. Hobbes et ux. Order affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff first class township had sued out a scire facias sur to enforce a municipal lien against defendant property owners. The owners defended under § 7 of the Municipal Claims Act of May 16, 1923, P.L. 207, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 7141. The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) entered an order that made absolute the township's rule for judgment for want of a sufficient affidavit of defense. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: In defense of the township's claim against the owners for the cost construction of a sidewalk in front of their premises, the owners claimed that the township gave them no notice and no opportunity to construct their own sidewalk as is required by § 7 of the Municipal Claims Act of May 16, 1923, P.L. 207, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 7141. The township contended that § 7 had been superseded by § 2303 of The First Class Township Code of June 24, 1931, P.L. 1206, as amended, May 27, 1949, P.L. 1955, Pa. Stat. The common pleas court made absolute a rule for judgment for the township on its motion for a judgment for want of a sufficient affidavit of defense, which the court held was a final appealable order. In upholding the judgment on review, the court held that the Township Code did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 7 because it was not local or special legislation; rather, the Township Code provision had been made a general law by reason of Pa. Const. art. III, § 34.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

In re Kovalchuk


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


202 Pa. Super. 389; 195 A.2d 828; 1962 Pa. Super. LEXIS 456


Argued November 11, 1963  
December 12, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 276, April T., 1963, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Oct. T., 1963, No. 59, in re suspension of restaurant liquor license number R-4434 issued to Walter Thomas Kovalchuk, trading as Mill Cafe and Restaurant. Order affirmed.

Appeal by licensee from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board suspending liquor license.

Order entered dismissing appeal and affirming decision of Board, opinion by WEISS, J. Licensee appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of an order of Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the licensee's appeal and affirmed a board's decision suspending the licensee's restaurant liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The licensee's restaurant liquor license was suspended because he allowed a female to serve liquor from behind a bar in violation of § 493(25) of the Liquor Code of April 12, 1951, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-493(25). The trial court affirmed the board's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. The legislation was not without a basis in reason.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

634 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Pewatts


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


200 Pa. Super. 22; 186 A.2d 408; 1962 Pa. Super. LEXIS 460


Argued November 14, 1962  
December 12, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 218 April T., 1962, from order of County Court of Allegheny County, No. 296 of 1962, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. John Pewatts, also known as John Pewats. Order affirmed.

Nonsupport. Before MCBRIDE, J.

Order entered directing natural father to pay stated weekly sum for support of illegitimate child. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that required him to pay child support for an illegitimate child after his obligation to pay child support that was issued in connection with a fornication and bastardy conviction had expired.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of fornication and bastardy by a court of quarter sessions, and he was ordered to pay child support up to the time that the child reached 14 years of age. Thus, when the child reached that age, defendant refused to pay further support. However, pursuant to § 732 of the 1939 Penal Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4732, the Commonwealth obtained an order requiring the father to support his illegitimate child after the child reached 14 years of age. Upon appeal, the trial court's order was affirmed. The court held that there were no limits to the father's obligation to support his child. Thus, the obligation of the father to support his child was merely suspended while he was paying child support pursuant to the order that was issued in the fornication and bastardy proceedings. The court also ruled that the father's obligation to pay support to the child after the child became 14 did not place defendant under jeopardy twice and did not subject him to cruel or unusual punishment. Also, the court held that § 4732 was not improperly applied to him retroactively. Thus, no constitutional rights of defendant were violated by the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

635 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cabell


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


199 Pa. Super. 513; 185 A.2d 611; 1962 Pa. Super. LEXIS 586


Argued September 10, 1962  
November 15, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 46, 47, 48, and 49, Oct. T., 1962, from orders of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, Jan. T., 1960, Nos. 1270, 1271, and 1272, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Robert A. Cabell, and Same v. George Dayton Luck. Orders reversed.

Indictment charging defendants with conspiracy to violate § 10-108(1) of Philadelphia Home Rule Charter and with making false statement and mark in civil service examination.

Orders entered granting defendants' motions to quash indictments, opinion by REIMEL, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The orders of the court below are reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth sought review of orders of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted both defendants' motions to quash indictments against them for conspiracy to violate Philadelphia, Pa., Home Rule Charter § 10-108(1) and for making false statements and marks in a civil service examination.


OVERVIEW: One of the defendants paid the other defendant to take a civil service examination on his behalf. They were indicted jointly for conspiracy, and each defendant was indicted separately for making false statements and marks in the examination. The court reversed the order that granted defendants' motions to quash all three indictments. The city was authorized to impose fines and imprisonment in Philadelphia, Pa., Home Rule Charter § 10-109 because the penalty was specifically authorized by § 17 of the Enabling Act (Act), 53 P.S. § 13131. The court held that the Act did not unconstitutionally delegate to the city the legislative power to create a crime because the city's police power included the right to pass and enforce ordinances. The city imposed the penalty for the proper municipal purpose of enforcing its civil service provisions. The court ruled that the necessary procedural safeguards were observed because the violation was a misdemeanor prosecuted with the safeguards incidental to a plenary criminal proceeding. The court held that the delegation of authority to the city was proper and constitutional and that the city's authority was properly exercised.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court that had quashed the indictments against defendants for conspiracy and for violating the city charter by making false statements and marks in the civil service examination.

Sayre Land Co. v. Pa. Public Util. Com


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


196 Pa. Super. 417; 175 A.2d 307; 1961 Pa. Super. LEXIS 505


September 13, 1961, Argued  
November 16, 1961, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Sayre Land Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com., 409 Pa. 356, 185 A.2d 325, 1962 Pa. LEXIS 454 (1962)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 7, March T., 1961, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, No. 2117 Equity Docket 1954, No. 150 1/2 Commonwealth Docket, 1954, in case of The Sayre Land Company v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Decree reversed.

Equity to enjoin Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission from entertaining jurisdiction over plaintiff as a public utility. Before SOHN, J.

Adjudication filed finding for the defendant; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and final decree entered. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed and the case is remanded with instructions to the court below to enter a proper decree as prayed for in the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of the decree of Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) which ruled in favor of defendant utility commission in the corporation's action to enjoin the commission from entertaining jurisdiction over it as a public utility.


OVERVIEW: In 1870 and 1871, 738 acres of land were purchased for the erection of commercial and residential buildings. The corporation was created for purchasing and improving real estate and selling the same in lots or parcels. Proceedings were instituted against the corporation by the utility commission, and the corporation filed a complaint seeking a permanent injunction compelling the utility commission to dismiss all proceedings. The trial court ruled in favor of the utility commission, and the corporation sought review. The court reversed because the 1937 Public Utility Law did not make the corporation a public utility merely because it owned property which it had leased to a public utility, there was no reason to make an exception to the basic doctrine of corporate entity, and the great portion of the corporation's business, rental and sale of real estate, could not be regulated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree and remanded the case to the court below to enter a proper decree as prayed for in the complaint.

Insurance Dep't v. Philadelphia


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania

638 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Tate Liquor License Case


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


196 Pa. Super. 193; 173 A.2d 657; 1961 Pa. Super. LEXIS 455


Argued June 13, 1961  
September 12, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 230, Oct. T., 1961, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Montgomery County, Nov. T., 1959, No. 84, in the matter of issuance of restaurant liquor license to Charles E. Tate, trading as North Hills Tavern. Order reversed.

Appeal by applicant from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board refusing application for restaurant liquor license but granting application for transfer of malt beverage license.

Order entered sustaining appeal and directing issuance of liquor license, opinion by HONEYMAN, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed, and the liquor license is refused.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Montgomery County, Nov. T., 1959 (Pennsylvania), which reversed a decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board refusing appellee applicant's request for a restaurant liquor license on grounds that amendment to § 404 of the Pennsylvania Liquor Code of April 12, 1951, P.L. 90, under which the request was refused, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court of quarter sessions held that the amendment to § 404 of the Liquor Code was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power. In the amendment to § 404 of the Liquor Code, the legislature delegated to the Board the power to determine whether selling liquor at a new establishment in certain neighborhoods would be detrimental to the inhabitants in a 500-foot radius of the premises. The court reversed the court of quarter sessions' order because the delegation was valid, the evidence supported the board's finding that the license would be detrimental, and the board did not abuse its discretion. Although the legislature could not delegate its power to make a law, it could confer authority in connection with the execution of the law. That was what the amendment to § 404 of the Liquor Code did. It gave the Board the authority to determine the fact of whether issuance of a liquor license would be detrimental to a neighborhood. The Board determined that it was, and the court had to apply the law as set forth in § 404 of the Liquor Code.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of quarter sessions' order and refused the liquor license.

 

639 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Blasi v. Alexander


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


195 Pa. Super. 634; 171 A.2d 904; 1961 Pa. Super. LEXIS 690


Argued March 22, 1961  
June 15, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 103, Oct. T., 1961, from decree of Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Dec. T., 1956, No. 1767, in case of C. J. Blasi v. Charles Alexander er al. Decree reversed.

Action to quiet title to real estate. Before SWENEY, P.J., without a jury.

Adjudication filed finding for defendants; exceptions to adjudication sustained and final decree entered. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The decree of the court below is reversed and the complaint and the record is remanded to the court below for the purpose of a decree in favor of the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant heirs appealed the decree of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania) that was entered in favor of plaintiff purchasers. The purchasers had brought an action to quiet title to certain real estate they purchased at a tax foreclosure sale. The heirs were the surviving children and the legal heirs of the owner of the property, who had died.


OVERVIEW: Two of the heirs were living at the property at issue. No notice of the tax sale was sent or delivered to any of the heirs. The notice was directed to the estate of the heirs' father in care of the wife of one of the heirs. A young child of one of the heirs signed the registered mail notice. The lower court determined that the provisions of the General County Assessment Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 5020-417 (1933), with regard to notice to the terre-tenant of the property, were not complied with. Therefore, the tax sale was invalid. The court agreed and held that a valid sale for unpaid taxes was not possible without some form of notice to the owner or the terre-tenant of the property. The court found that the tax assessor had not ascertained the owner of the real estate, even with having some knowledge of a change of ownership because of addressing the notice to an estate. The court held that there was no evidence that notice actually reached any of the heirs with the notice having been addressed to the estate of the deceased owner and delivered to a child. As a result, the court held that the tax sale under which the purchasers claimed title was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case to the lower court for the purpose of entering a decree in favor of the heirs.

 

640 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Gribbel v. Donoian


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


193 Pa. Super. 445; 165 A.2d 410; 1960 Pa. Super. LEXIS 680


Argued September 12, 1960  
November 16, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 200, Oct. T., 1960, from order of Municipal Court of Philadelphia, July T., 1959, No. 1119, in case of John Gribbel, II v. George Donoian. Order affirmed.

Appeal by defendant from judgment in action of trespass for property damage entered by magistrate.

Defendant's petition for special leave to file appeal dismissed; plaintiff's motion to strike off appeal refused, opinion by BOYLE, J. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order of the Municipal Court of Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, which dismissed its motion to strike off an appeal filed by defendant in plaintiff's action of trespass for property damage in which plaintiff had recovered judgment and defendant had appealed. Plaintiff argued that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 42, § 913a (1956) violated the Pennsylvania Constitution by restricting the right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action in trespass and recovered judgment. Defendant appealed, and plaintiff filed a motion to strike off the appeal on the ground that § 913a limited the right of appeal from a magistrate's judgment to cases where the judgment was in excess of $ 100. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's motion, holding that § 913a did not apply to appeals from magistrates to municipal courts. Plaintiff appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that it could sustain the trial court's decision for a different reason than that which was assigned and that § 913a was in plain conflict with the mandate of Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 (1894). The effect of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 42, § 913a (1956) was to prohibit appeals as a matter of right where the judgment given by a magistrate, alderman, or justice of the peace did not exceed $ 100, excluding costs. The provision in § 913a for appeals on "special allowance" did not save it because the right of trial by jury was not a matter of judicial discretion. The Pennsylvania Legislature could not constitutionally impose any provisions substantially restrictive of the sacred and inherent right of trial by jury, which was to remain inviolate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

641 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Upsey v. Secretary of Revenue


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


193 Pa. Super. 466; 165 A.2d 267; 1960 Pa. Super. LEXIS 684


Argued September 14, 1960  
November 16, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 182, Oct. T., 1960, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1960, No. 939, in the matter of Elbert Upsey v. Secretary of Revenue, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Order affirmed.

Appeal by licensee from decision of Secretary of Revenue suspending motor vehicle operating license.

Order entered dismissing appeal, opinion by CHUDOFF, J. Licensee appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) sustaining a decision of appellee, the Pennsylvania Secretary of Revenue, suspending the driver's motor vehicle operating license pursuant to § 618 of the Vehicle Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 75, § 618, after he was arrested for operating his motor vehicle under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: Upon the driver's arrest for driving while intoxicated, the Secretary held a hearing to determine whether his operating license should be suspended. The driver objected to the same while the criminal charge was pending. The Secretary suspended the driver's operating license, and the trial court sustained that decision. On appeal, the court held that the license revocation penalty in § 616 of the Vehicle Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 75, § 616, and the license suspension penalty in § 618 of the Code could apply to the same offense. The legislature authorized the Secretary to suspend the license of an operator for the same offense for which it provided for a mandatory revocation. There was nothing in the state or federal constitutions to prevent a double penalty. The court held that it was not double jeopardy under Pa. Const. art. I, § 10 and did not violate the Due Process Clause of the federal constitution to apply the penalties of both § 616 and § 618 of the Code to the same violation. The court further held that the Secretary's action did not violate Pa. Const. art. I, § 9, relating to self-incrimination, or the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

642 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Whalan v. Banmiller


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


192 Pa. Super. 134; 160 A.2d 126; 1960 Pa. Super. LEXIS 428



April 13, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 295, Miscellaneous Docket No. 6; petition for leave to file appeal without payment of statutory filing fee, in case of Commonwealth ex rel. Edward J. Whalen v. William J. Banmiller, Warden. Petition refused.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, brought a petition for leave to file an appeal without payment of the statutory filing fee in a habeas corpus case.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner in a habeas corpus case filed a petition for leave to file appeal without payment of the statutory filing fee. The court denied the petition. The court found that the statute requiring the payment of filing fees, the Pennsylvania Act of May 19, 1897, P.L. 67, § 3, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 12, § 1135, was constitutional as applied to appeals in habeas corpus cases. Also, the court noted that the prisoner was in a Pennsylvania State penitentiary. As a prisoner in such an institution he received an allowance from the Commonwealth. Since the prisoner returned to the penitentiary as a convicted parole violator he received about $ 330. Although he spent all of it except about $ 5, had he not spent it he would have been able to pay the $ 12 filing fee. Under these circumstances the Commonwealth did not foreclose the prisoner access to the court. Finally, the prisoner's latest conviction was reviewed by the court. The prisoner brought this habeas corpus action raising substantially the same questions previously presented while the review of his conviction and sentence were pending before the Supreme Court. If indigent, the prisoner was not entitled to overlapping free reviews.


OUTCOME: The court denied the prisoner leave to file an appeal without payment of the statutory filing fee.

Overmiller v. D. E. Horn & Co.


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


191 Pa. Super. 562; 159 A.2d 245; 1960 Pa. Super. LEXIS 384


Argued December 16, 1959.  
March 24, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 20, March T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas of York County, Aug. T., 1956, No. 314, in case of W. Luther Overmiller v. D. E. Horn & Co., Inc. et al. Order reversed.

Appeal by employer and its carrier from decision of Workmen's Compensation Board allowing a rehearing to claimant and remanding record.

Order entered dismissing appeal, opinion by ANDERSON, P.J. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the board granting a rehearing is reversed, and the case remitted to the court below for the entry of such order by it.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania) which concluded that the order of the Workmen's Compensation Board directing a rehearing of plaintiff employee's claim was interlocutory and dismissed the employer's appeal from the board's ruling.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a workers' compensation claim, which a referee disallowed. The employee appealed to the Workmen's Compensation Board, but withdrew his appeal. Over one year later, he filed a petition for a rehearing, which the board granted. The employer appealed to the court of common pleas, which dismissed the appeal holding that order was interlocutory. On appeal, the court reversed and remitted for an order reversing the grant of a rehearing. The court held that the board lacked authority to consider the employee's petition for rehearing because it was filed too late and was barred by § 426 of The Pennsylvania Workmen's Compensation Act, 1915 Pa. Laws 736, as last amended by 77 P.S. § 871 . The amendment was not intended to apply retroactively to petitions filed before its effective date. The statute was a statute of repose that had to be applied prospectively. The board's power to entertain a petition for review ceased after one year after its last order. The legislature could not have revived such a claim even if it had intended to. Although such an interlocutory order would not usually have been appealable, the board considered the petition in violation of its authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Workmen's Compensation Board granting a rehearing to the employee, and remitted the case for the entry of such order in favor of the employer.
