Dunn Appeal


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


191 Pa. Super. 346; 156 A.2d 349; 1959 Pa. Super. LEXIS 540


Argued April 13, 1959.  
December 17, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 51, April T., 1959, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Mercer County, June T., 1958, No. 57, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Joseph Marek. Order reversed.

Proceeding upon petition and rule to show cause why costs imposed on petitioner by grand jury should not be set aside.

Order entered discharging rule, opinion by McKAY, J. Petitioner appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed, and the rule to set aside the imposition of costs is made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mayor appealed from an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which refused to set aside its order imposing costs on him for grand jury proceedings involving respondents, a district attorney and a county.


OVERVIEW: A fraternal organization was charged with setting up a lottery and possessing gambling devices. The grand jury ignored the resulting bills of indictment and placed the costs on the mayor as the real prosecutor. The mayor had ordered the raid, but his name was not endorsed on the indictments as the prosecutor, and he was not called as a witness before the grand jury. The court reversed the order below, finding that the mayor could not be required to pay the grand jury's costs under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 1222 (1860). The court held that due process required that the mayor be before the grand jury, as a prosecutor or as a witness, before he could be ordered to pay costs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order below. The rule to set aside the imposition of costs was made absolute.

Commonwealth v. Stone


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


191 Pa. Super. 117; 155 A.2d 453; 1959 Pa. Super. LEXIS 500


Argued September 14, 1959.  
November 11, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 32 to 36, inclusive, March T., 1960, from orders of Court of Quarter Sessions of Dauphin County, June T., 1958, Nos. 57 to 61, inclusive, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Stanley S. Stone et al. Orders affirmed.

Indictments charging defendants with engaging in budget planning business.

Defendants' motion to quash indictments sustained, opinion by KREIDER, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff the Commonwealth sought review of orders of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) sustaining defendants' motion to quash indictments that charged defendants with engaging in budget planning business in violation of The Act of 1955, P.L. 755, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4897.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were budget planners. As a result of their activity, defendants were indicted for violating The Act of 1955, P.L. 755 (Pennsylvania), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4897, which made the act of engaging in budget planning a misdemeanor. Defendants filed a motion to quash the indictments on the ground that § 4897 was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the motion, and the Commonwealth appealed the decision contending that it was erroneous. The Commonwealth argued that § 4897 was a proper exercise of its police power to protect citizens from potentially illegal conduct of budget planners. The court noted that for an exercise of the police power to be valid the law must not be unreasonable, unduly oppressive, or patently beyond the necessities of the case, and the means which it employed must have a real and substantial relation to the objects sought to have been obtained. Since § 4897 prohibited all budget planning activity under the theory that there might somewhere, sometime be a dishonest budget planner, the court held that this was not a proper exercise of the police power. Section 4897 was properly declared unconstitutional, and the orders were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

646 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Haun v. Cavell


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


190 Pa. Super. 346; 154 A.2d 257; 1959 Pa. Super. LEXIS 649


Argued June 12, 1959  
September 16, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 115, April T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County, Sept. T., 1958, No. 92, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Charles Haun v. Angelo C. Cavell, Warden. Order reversed.

Habeas corpus.

Order entered granting writ and directing release of relator, opinion by RODGERS, P.J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order and decree of the court below granting the writ of habeas corpus is reversed and the petition for the writ is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth, by and through its attorney general, appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which directed the discharge of appellee prisoner after he commenced a proceeding in habeas corpus to obtain his release from a state penitentiary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced for felonious assault to the state penitentiary for a term of 3 to 6 years. After completing his minimum sentence, defendant was paroled by the parole board to serve "back time." At the expiration of that term, the parole board recommitted defendant to the state penitentiary as a parole violator. Defendant commenced a habeas corpus proceeding to obtain his release from the state penitentiary. The lower court directed that the defendant be discharged. The Commonwealth, by and through its attorney general, appealed and the court reversed the order and dismissed the petition. The court held that what the legislature must have intended by "at liberty on parole" was not at liberty from all confinement but at liberty from confinement on the particular sentence for which defendant was reentered as a parole violator. The court noted that if the legislature intended to change this policy, it would have done so directly, and that such a change should not have been inferred by interpretation of a provision in 61 P.S. § 331.21a that made no reference to the credits to have been given a parole violator who served time on other offenses after reentry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and dismissed the petition for the writ.

Milk Maid Dairy Products, Inc. v. Milk Control Com.


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


190 Pa. Super. 410; 154 A.2d 274; 1959 Pa. Super. LEXIS 659


Argued June 9, 1959  
September 16, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 188, Oct. T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1958, No. 414, in case of Milk Maid Dairy Products, Inc. v. Milk Control Commission of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Order reversed.

Appeal by milk dealer from decision of Milk Control Commission suspending milk dealer's license.

Order entered sustaining appeal, opinion by REIMEL, J. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below is reversed, and the order of the commission is reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Pennsylvania Milk Control Commission, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 5 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which reversed an order by which the Commission suspended appellee milk dealer's license for violating the Commission's Rules of Trade Practices. The Commission found that the dealer had lent refrigerator equipment, free of charge, to many of its wholesale customers.


OVERVIEW: The trial court accepted the contention that Rule of Trade Practices A-1 was unreasonable and illegal. On appeal by the Commission, the court did not agree with the trial court that the Rule failed to meet the test of constitutionality. The court held that the dealer had failed to show that the Rule was unconstitutional. The purpose of the Milk Control Law of April 28, 1937 was to assure a sufficient supply of pure milk, primarily through price regulation and control. The court also held that the constitutionality of the Law seemed to be firmly established. To maintain an established price, it was necessary to prevent a seller, such as the dealer, from giving to a purchaser anything of value in addition to the milk. When the dealer furnished the refrigeration equipment, the wholesalers could sell the milk below the fixed price. The amount of money involved was not de minimis, as the cost of milk refrigeration was substantial. The court did not agree with the dealer that its loaned equipment had no relation to maintaining an established milk price. Because the dealer admitted its violation, the court had no alternative but to reinstate the Commission's order suspending the dealer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and affirmed the order of the Commission by which the dealer's license was suspended.

Philadelphia Tax Review Board v. Norton, Lilly & Co.


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


189 Pa. Super. 91; 149 A.2d 672; 1959 Pa. Super. LEXIS 372


Argued December 17, 1958.  
March 20, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 1, Oct. T., 1959, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, Sept. T., 1957, No. 2122, in case of City of Philadelphia Tax Review Board v. Norton, Lilly & Co. Order reversed.

Appeal by taxpayer from decision of Tax Review Board denying petitions for review of mercantile license tax assessment.

Order entered dismissing exceptions and affirming decision of board, before GRIFFITHS and CHUDOFF, JJ., opinion by GRIFFITHS, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Decision reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas, Number One, of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of appellee city tax board and dismissed the taxpayer's exceptions to the board's decision denying the taxpayer's petition for review of a mercantile license tax assessment.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a corporation that engaged in the business of a general steamship agent, and it argued that the city tax was unconstitutional and invalid under U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, the Commerce Clause, and U. S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 2, the Import-export Clause. In reversing, the court agreed. First, the court noted that the taxpayer's business was to solicit cargo for shipment by steamship and passenger travel and that it also exercised a degree of control over the loading and unloading of cargo and the berthing and dispatching of vessels. Applying precedent, the court noted that such activities were incident to the movement of cargo and thus constituted a continuation of the transport of goods in interstate and foreign commerce. Next, the court found that the tax on the taxpayer's gross receipts was an impermissible tax upon the commerce itself and was, therefore, invalid under the Commerce Clause. In addition, the court found that the tax on the taxpayer's gross receipts violated the Import-export Clause, which prohibited any state from laying duties on imports or exports except as to costs necessary to cover the state's inspection laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and the decision of the board.

Nester Appeal


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


187 Pa. Super. 313; 144 A.2d 623; 1958 Pa. Super. LEXIS 679


Argued March 24, 1958  
September 11, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 106, Oct. T., 1958, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Montgomery County, June T., 1957, No. 13, in re petition of electors of Borough of Pottstown and of the ten wards therein for reapportionment and consolidation of said wards. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon petition of registered elector to dismiss petition of electors requesting consolidation of borough wards.

Order entered dismissing petition of elector and order entered appointing commission pursuant to petition for consolidation, opinion by GERBER, J. Elector appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought review of the decision of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which found in favor of appellee electors and refused to dismiss the electors' petition brought under the Act of May 4, 1927, P.L. 519, § 601 et seq., as amended by The Borough Code of July 10, 1947, P.L. 1621 and subsequent acts, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 45601 et seq.


OVERVIEW: A petition was presented to the court of quarter sessions by the requisite number of electors of the borough alleging that the borough's 20 member council was the largest legislative body in the Commonwealth excepting only the General Assembly, and praying that the existing ten wards be consolidated. The resident filed a petition under the Act of March 5, 1925, P.L. 23, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 12, § 672, asking that the electors' petition be dismissed for lack of jurisdiction on the ground that the statutory provision authorizing the court to consolidate the borough wards was unconstitutional. The court below, refused to dismiss the electors' petition. The court affirmed, concluding that: (1) an act of the legislature should not be declared unconstitutional unless it violated the Constitution clearly, palpably, and plainly; (2) the courts' decisions setting out the procedure to be followed constituted the law governing the application of The Borough Code, 1947 P.L. 1621, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 45601 et seq.; and (3) the resident failed to discharge the heavy burden placed upon him to overcome the strong presumption of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order refusing to dismiss the electors' petition for consolidation of the existing wards in the petition brought by the resident.

 

651 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


In re Tahiti Bar, Inc.


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


186 Pa. Super. 214; 142 A.2d 491; 1958 Pa. Super. LEXIS 463


Argued March 26, 1958.  
June 11, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 268, Oct. T., 1957, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, Nov. T., 1956, No. 1122, in the matter of Tahiti Bar, Incorporated. Order affirmed.

Appeal by licensee from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board suspending restaurant liquor license and amusement permit.

Order entered dismissing appeal, opinion by SLOANE, J. Licensee appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which found in favor of appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board and dismissed the licensee's appeal from a suspension order.


OVERVIEW: The licensee, a bar, provided entertainment which consisted of various dance routines described as "bumps and grinds" by female entertainers who had removed practically all of their clothing. The court below found as a fact that the entertainment was lewd, immoral or improper and that the entertainment was a predominant appeal to prurient interest. On appeal, the licensee argued that that the language in the Pennsylvania Liquor Code § 493, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-493 was unconstitutionally vague, that the entertainment was not obscene, and that it was entitled to a jury trial. The court affirmed, concluding that: (1) the words used in the Liquor Code, when taken together, were sufficiently clear to enable any ordinary person to understand what kind of entertainment was proscribed; (2) the entertainment, as shown by undisputed evidence, was lewd or obscene as well as immoral under any definition of these terms; and (3) the revocation of a liquor license did not give rise to a right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board which dismissed the licensee's appeal from a suspension order.

Commonwealth ex rel. Bozzi v. Myers


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


186 Pa. Super. 42; 140 A.2d 375; 1958 Pa. Super. LEXIS 423


Argued March 25, 1958.  
April 16, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 139, Oct. T., 1958, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 3 of Philadelphia County, March T., 1957, No. 9797, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. James Bozzi v. David N. Myers, Warden. Order affirmed.

Habeas corpus.

Order entered dismissing petition, opinion by GRIFFITHS, J. Relator appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator prisoner appealed the judgment by the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of felonious possession of drugs, and his sentence was enhanced by a prior conviction. The prisoner was sentenced to a term in the county prison. Because of overcrowding, the prisoner was transferred to the State penitentiary. The prisoner sought a writ of habeas corpus, and argued that the transfer to the penitentiary was improper. The trial court dismissed the petition. On the prisoner's appeal, the court affirmed. While imprisonment in the penitentiary was considered more severe than imprisonment in the county jail, there was no provision which permitted the court to reduce the prisoner's sentence on that basis. In fact, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 75 prohibited a reduction in sentence based on a transfer. There was no due process violation because the prisoner had no vested property right to remain in the county jail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

654 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Bristow


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


185 Pa. Super. 448; 138 A.2d 156; 1958 Pa. Super. LEXIS 811


Argued October 9, 1957  
January 21, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 14, Oct. T., 1958, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Franklin County, Oct. T., 1956, No. 106, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Val S. Bristow. Order reversed; reargument refused February 10, 1958.

Indictment charging defendant with sale of fireworks in violation of the Act of May 15, 1939, P.L. 134. Before DEPUY, J.

Verdict of guilty; defendant's motion in arrest of judgment granted. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order in arrest of judgment is reversed, and the record is remitted to the court below for consideration and proper disposition of defendant's motion for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania appealed from an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Franklin County (Pennsylvania), which granted defendant's motion in arrest of judgment, following a verdict of guilty upon an indictment charging defendant with sale of fireworks in violation of the Act of May 15, 1939, P.L. 134.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted, tried, and convicted by a jury for the violation of the Act of May 15, 1939, P.L. 134, as amended, 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 1271 et seq., otherwise known as the Fireworks Law, which prohibited, except in certain cases, the sale, offering or exposing for sale and use of fireworks. The trial court granted defendant's motion in arrest of judgment, holding that the law was unconstitutional, as it related to the prohibition of the sale, the offering for sale, or the use of fireworks by the general public. On appeal, the court determined that, if its inquiry had been properly limited, the trial court would have found no basis for declaring the law unconstitutional on the grounds that it related to conduct which was beyond the police power of the legislature to prohibit, and that it was vague and indefinite. The court held that the toy cannons in defendant's case clearly came within the statutory definition of fireworks and that the prohibition of their sale was directly related to the promotion of the health, safety, and general welfare of the public. The court concluded that the statute was not vague and indefinite as it applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order in arrest of judgment and remitted the case to the trial court for consideration and proper disposition of defendant's motion for a new trial.

 

655 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Coe v. Duffield


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


185 Pa. Super. 532; 138 A.2d 303; 1958 Pa. Super. LEXIS 821


Argued November 11, 1957  
January 21, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 122 and 123, April T., 1957, from orders of Court of Common Pleas of Greene County, Nos. 457 and 458 of 1957, in cases of Durward Coe et al. v. C. Paul Duffield et al., and Kenneth L. Headlee et al. v. C. Paul Duffield et al. Orders affirmed.

Complaints in equity. Before HOOK, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding for defendants; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and orders entered dismissing complaints. Plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order dismissing the complaint is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owners filed complaints in equity to restrain defendant school district from collecting an amusement tax on pinball machines and admissions to drive-in theaters and roller skating rinks. The business owners alleged that the tax violated the uniform tax provisions of Pa. Const. art. 9, § 1. The Court of Common Pleas of Greene County (Pennsylvania) dismissed the complaints. The business owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The disputed school district tax imposed a $ 25 tax on pinball machines and a 10 percent tax on admissions to drive-in theaters and roller skating rinks. The business owners alleged that the imposition of the tax upon their businesses and not upon other forms of amusement for which admissions were charged within the territorial limits of the school district violated constitutional equal protection and uniform tax provisions. The court held that the classification of pinball machines and admissions to drive-in theaters and roller skating rinks was constitutionally permissible. The court held that the school district could distinguish between businesses so long as it did so in good faith and so long as the classification did not make an arbitrary or unjust distinction. The court held that the school district was not required to treat all forms of amusement in a similar fashion. The mere fact that the tax was imposed on only specific forms of amusement did not did not make the tax an unconstitutional or illegal tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Department of Highways v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


185 Pa. Super. 1; 136 A.2d 473; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 202


Argued March 11, 1957  
November 18, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 4, March T., 1957, from order of Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, February 14, 1956, No. 80979, in case of Department of Highways of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission et al. Order affirmed.

Proceeding upon application of Department of Highways for relocation and improvement of highway-railway crossings and for allocation of costs.

Order entered directing in part that the Department of Highways reimburse particular utility companies for 60% of their relocation costs. Department of Highways appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff highway department appealed a decision from defendant Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission (commission) ordering the highway department to reimburse the light company and the gas company for the costs they incurred relocating their facilities due to a highway department construction project.


OVERVIEW: The highway department wanted to relocate and improve certain state highway routes. The highway department petitioned the commission for approval and for allocation of costs. The commission ordered the highway department to pay 60 percent of the costs incurred by the light company and the gas company for relocating their facilities. The highway department initiated an action challenging the commission's order. The court found that the Pennsylvania Public Utility Law, 66 P.S. § 1179, authorized the commission to impose upon the commonwealth the cost of relocating utilities pursuant to a highway construction project. The court held that the relocation of utility facilities fell within the term expense of such construction under 66 P.S. § 1181, so that the commonwealth was required to pay for the relocation. The court concluded that the highway department acted as an agent of the commonwealth and was subject to the payment of costs incident to the expense of relocation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision ordering the highway department to reimburse the gas company and the light company for their relocation costs.

Commonwealth v. Grochowiak


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


184 Pa. Super. 522; 136 A.2d 145; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 291; 33 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P71,153


Argued October 9, 1957  
November 12, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 8, Oct. T., 1958, from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Franklin County, Oct. T., 1956, No. 148, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Robert John Grochowiak. Judgment affirmed.

Appeal to quarter sessions by defendant from conviction before justice of the peace upon charge of exhibiting motion picture on Sunday in violation of the Act of 1935, P.L. 599. Before DEPUY, P.J., without a jury.

Finding of guilty and judgment of sentence entered thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and the defendant is ordered to appear at a time to be fixed by the lower court, for compliance with the sentence imposed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Franklin County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a judgment of conviction against him for violating the Act of July 2, 1935, P. L. 599, § 2 for showing movies on a Sunday.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the manager of a drive in theatre. The movies he showed on a Sunday were not religious in nature but they were not obscene or offensive. The content of the movies was not in dispute. Defendant argued that his conviction was unconstitutional. He specifically asserted that the Act was unconstitutional because it infringed upon the right of free speech. The court held that the Act was a restriction on free speech that merely limited the right as to time or place and therefore the restriction was valid. The State had the power to prohibit public amusements and exhibitions on Sundays. Defendant next contended that he was denied due process and equal protection. The court disagreed and determined that defendant's rights were not violated. Finally, defendant argued that the Act worked an unreasonable classification. The court concluded that the legislation was valid. Defendant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Summit Hill Rod & Gun Club Liquor License Case


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


184 Pa. Super. 584; 135 A.2d 781; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 303


Argued September 30, 1957  
November 12, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 193, Oct. T., 1957, from order of Court of Quarter Sessions of Carbon County, Oct. T., 1956, No. 57, in case of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board v. The Summit Hill Rod and Gun Club. Order reversed.

Appeal by licensee from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board suspending club liquor license. Before MCCREADY, P.J.

Order entered reversing board and setting aside suspension. Commonwealth appealed.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and the record is remanded to the court below for the imposition of a 15-day suspension to commence at a time to be fixed by that court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board, sought review of an order of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Carbon County (Pennsylvania), which set aside a decision of the Board that suspended the liquor license of appellee sporting club.


OVERVIEW: The Board instituted proceedings to suspend the club's liquor license on allegations that the club sold liquor and beer to non-members. The Board conducted a hearing and determined that the club had sold alcohol to non-members on two separate occasions. The Board imposed a 15-day suspension on the club's license. The trial court reversed the Board's decision, concluding that the Board had not proven its case by clear, precise, and indubitable evidence and that it did not find as a fact that the club sold liquor or malt and brewed beverages on the licensed premises. The trial court based its decision on the lack of evidence and the fact that no analysis was made of the beverage sold to enforcement officers to show that it was a malt or brewed beverage. The court reversed, holding that the trial court committed error in placing too great a burden of proof on the Board. The court stated that the Board's burden was based on civil rather than criminal proceedings, and it had the authority to revoke or suspend the club's license. The court determined that the decision was sufficient if the Board proved by a preponderance of the evidence that the license suspension was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.

United States v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


184 Pa. Super. 380; 135 A.2d 93; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 265


Argued November 15, 1956  
September 30, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 27, Oct. T., 1955, from orders of Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission at Investigation Docket No. 24, in case of United States of America v. The Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Orders affirmed.

Proceedings before Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission following institution by commission, on its own motion, of investigation to determine whether railroad was transporting property at charges other than as provided in its officially filed tariffs.

Order entered affirming prior order of commission, asserting jurisdiction over matter and enjoining railroad from charging rates other than those in its tariffs filed with commission. United States appealed.



DISPOSITION: The orders are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant United States sought review of an order entered by the trial court (Pennsylvania) affirming a prior order of appellee Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, which asserted jurisdiction over a matter involving tariffs charged by a railroad in violation of §§ 303 and 304 of the Public Utility Law of May 28, 1937, 66 P.S. §§ 1143, 1144, and enjoined it from charging rates other than those in its tariffs filed with the Commission.


OVERVIEW: The Commission, on its own motion, instituted an investigation to determine whether a railroad was transporting property at charges other than as provided in its officially filed tariffs. The Commission determined that the railroad was transporting property intrastate for the United States free of charge or at a lower rate than the filed tariffs, and it ordered the railroad to cease and desist from its practice. The court held that: (1) § 303 of the Law did not, by identifying its application to any person, corporation, or municipal corporation in requiring compliance with filed tariffs, exclude shipments of the United States; (2) the service furnished by the railroad to the United States was within the meaning of the Law and the rates charged were required to be filed with the Commission; and (3) the Law was constitutional and the mere fact that an increased economic burden was imposed on the United States by requiring the railroad to comply with its established tariffs was not a valid basis for bringing the railroad within an implied governmental immunity. The court held that the Commission had jurisdiction to order the railroad to comply with its established tariffs.


OUTCOME: Holding that the provisions of the Law relating to the power to regulate intrastate rates were constitutional and that the Commission had jurisdiction to enter the order requiring the railroad to comply with its established tariffs, the court affirmed the Commission's orders.

Tax Review Board v. C. J. Devine & Co.


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


184 Pa. Super. 297; 134 A.2d 238; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 251


Argued March 25, 1957  
July 25, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 89, Oct. T., 1957, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County, Dec. T., 1955, No. 2686, in case of Tax Review Board v. C.J. Devine & Co. Order affirmed.

Appeal by taxpayer from decision of Tax Review Board denying petitions for refund of mercantile license taxes.

Order entered dismissing appeal, opinion by BROWN, P.J. Taxpayer appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court below dismissing the appeal is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas No. 4 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed decisions of the Revenue Commissioner and Tax Review Board of Philadelphia to deny a refund of a mercantile license fee and mercantile taxes on the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a securities dealer with its principal place of business out of state and a branch office in Philadelphia. It was not required under § 2 of The Pennsylvania Securities Act of June 24, 1939, P.L. 748, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 70, § 31 et seq. to be licensed as a securities dealer in Pennsylvania. The city collected a mercantile license fee and mercantile taxes from the taxpayer under the Philadelphia Mercantile License Tax Ordinance, Philadelphia, Pa. Code of General Ordinances ch. 19-1000, for which the taxpayer sought a refund. The Revenue Commissioner of Philadelphia, the Tax Review Board of Philadelphia, and the trial court denied the refund. The court affirmed. The court held that the city could collect taxes from the taxpayer because the Sterling Act of Aug. 5, 1932, P.L. 45, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 4613, allowed such collection only against taxpayers or their property which were not subject to state tax or license fee. The city tax ordinance did not create an unconstitutional classification under Pa. Const. art. IX, § 1. Imposing the tax only on the taxpayer was proper because it was exempt from state tax and tended to equalize the tax burden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of refund of the mercantile license fee and mercantile taxes.

Commonwealth v. Blumenstein


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


184 Pa. Super. 83; 133 A.2d 865; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 215


Argued April 8, 1957  
June 22, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 1, Feb. T., 1958, from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Lackawanna County, Dec. T., 1956, No. 8, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Martin Blumenstein. Judgment affirmed.

Indictment charging defendant with giving and permitting exhibition of moving pictures of a lascivious, obscene, indecent and immoral character and tending to corrupt morals. Before EAGEN, J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence entered thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, and it is ordered that appellant appear in the court below at such time as he may be there called, and that he be by that court committed until he has complied with his sentence or any part thereof which had not been performed at the time the order of supersedeas was entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Court of Quarter Sessions of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania) for giving and permitting exhibition of films of a lascivious, obscene, indecent, and immoral character and tending to corrupt morals in violation of § 528 of The Penal Code, the Act of June 24, 1939, P.L. 872, § 528, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4528.


OVERVIEW: Defendant managed a movie theater. An uncut version of a film, which had previously been refused approval by the Pennsylvania State Board of Censors, was exhibited at the theater. The trial court found that the film depicted a series of dancing acts, which were cheap, lewd, obscene, and indecent. On appeal, defendant argued that the film did not constitute an exhibition in violation of § 528. In addition, he argued that § 528 was unconstitutional because it contained no definition of the conduct proscribed and because the language of § 528 was so broad that its sanctions applied to conduct within the protection of U.S. Const. amend. I, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Pa. Const. art. I. The court found that the finding of the trial court that the film was obscene was supported by the evidence. Section 528 was not unconstitutional. The words used in § 528 had well-settled connotations that could be applied by the exercise of ordinary common sense and reason. The type of films that could be lawfully exhibited could be restricted. The right of free speech was not absolute. Lewd, obscene, and indecent speech could be prevented and punished without raising any constitutional problem.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for giving and permitting exhibition of films of a lascivious, obscene, indecent, and immoral character and tending to corrupt morals.

Commonwealth v. Cushard


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


184 Pa. Super. 193; 132 A.2d 366; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 230


Argued November 17, 1956  
June 11, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 226, April T., 1956, from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Allegheny County, June T., 1956, No. 643, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Edgar M. Cushard, Sr. Judgment affirmed.

Information charging defendant with threatening to do harm. Before SOFFEL, J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Quarter Sessions of the Peace of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of threatening to do harm to another.


OVERVIEW: The charge was based on a telephone call. The prosecutrix testified that defendant not only identified himself but that she recognized his voice. He stated to her that he would get her. She further testified that she was put in fear by the threat because of the knowledge that defendant had beaten his wife and that she was afraid that she would get similar treatment. Defendant was convicted. The trial court ordered him to post a surety bond. Defendant contended that the Act of March 31, 1860, P.L. 427, § 6, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 23, and the Act of March 18, 1909, P.L. 42, § 1, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 24, were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that where there was a malicious intent to do harm and the prosecutrix was put in fear of her safety, the law did not require an actual assault before affording protection. The expression "I'll get you," together with the background information, fairly led to the conclusion that it was not intended merely as a friendly gesture. The Act of 1909 qualified the Act of 1860, by establishing a standard under which the Act of 1860 should operate. The standard created was a reasonable one. The Acts were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

664 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Harrison


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


183 Pa. Super. 133; 130 A.2d 198; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 322


Argued November 12, 1956  
March 20, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 13 and 14, April T., 1956, from judgments of County Court of Allegheny County, 1955, Nos. C857, and C821, in cases of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, City of Pittsburgh, v. David M. Harrison. Judgments affirmed.

Proceedings upon informations charging defendant with violations of The Vehicle Code. Before LENCHER, P.J.

Judgments entered adjudging defendant guilty and fixing sentences. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence are affirmed, and the record is remitted to the court below, and it is ordered that defendant appear in the court below at such time as he may there be called, and that he be by that court committed until he has complied with the sentences, or any parts thereof which have not been performed at the time each appeal was made a supersedeas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which adjudged him guilty and fixed sentences in proceedings upon informations charging him with failure to obey the signals or directions of officers in violation of section 1218 (d) of the Pa. Vehicle Code of May 1, 1929, P.L. 905, as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 75, § 783(d).


OVERVIEW: On two separate occasions, defendant was attempting to make a right turn at an intersection. Because of the congested conditions, the officer at each intersection directed defendant to proceed through. Defendant refused to obey the officers' orders. Defendant contended that no statute or ordinance specifically precluded a right turn at those intersections and that to permit the judgment of an individual police officer to supersede the traffic statutes and ordinances was an unlawful delegation of legislative power and thus unconstitutional. The court held that the officers had authority to direct defendant to proceed straight through the intersections under the conditions of traffic existing at the time of these offenses. While it was true that an ordinance making some specific regulation of traffic, such as prohibiting a right turn at all or at designated times, was unenforceable unless the requisite signs were posted, it did not follow that the specific authority of a police officer had to be posted on an official sign before he could act to direct traffic in an emergency or to expedite congested traffic. The city acted within the limits prescribed by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of sentence.

Paper Products Co. v. Pittsburgh


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


183 Pa. Super. 234; 130 A.2d 219; 1957 Pa. Super. LEXIS 335


Argued November 19, 1956  
March 20, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 224, April T., 1956, from judgment of County Court of Allegheny County, 1953, No. A1360, in case of Paper Products Company, Inc. v. The City of Pittsburgh et al. Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Appeal by plaintiff from reassessments for mercantile license taxes. Before LENCHER, P.J.

Adjudication filed finding for tax authorities; exceptions to adjudication dismissed and judgment entered against plaintiff. Plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the court below is affirmed in part and reversed in part and the case is remitted for the entry of judgment in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment by the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that found in favor of respondent city in action by the city for reassessments for mercantile license taxes.


OVERVIEW: The city reassessed mercantile taxes upon the taxpayer. The taxpayer refused to pay the taxes and judgment was entered in favor of the city. The taxpayer appealed from the decision. The court stated the issue was whether the taxpayer made certain sales as a wholesale dealer or vendor, or whether it made them as a retail dealer or vendor, as those terms are used in the Mercantile License Tax Act of June 20, 1947, P.L. 745, Section 1, 24 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 582.1 et seq. The court found that the toilet paper, napkins, cups and similar products which were sold by the taxpayer and used by the purchasers, or their employees, on their own premises should be classified as retail business for the purpose of determining the tax rate regardless of whether they were sold to a merchant, physician or any other person. Because the record was inadequate regarding the taxpayer's sale, the court made a determination of what sales constituted wholesale transactions and what sales constituted retail transactions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

666 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth ex rel. Keiffer v. Ceraul


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


182 Pa. Super. 511; 128 A.2d 187; 1956 Pa. Super. LEXIS 425


Submitted October 5, 1956  
December 28, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 12, Oct. T., 1957, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, Sept. T., 1956, No. 60, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. William F. Keiffer v. Thomas Ceraul, Warden, Northampton County Prison. Judgment reversed.

Habeas corpus. Before WOODRING, J.

Order entered discharging writ. Relator appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and the prisoner discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus against appellee prison warden. The prisoner had been serving a sentence of two years imposed by a county alderman on a guilty plea to a charge of assault and battery. The prisoner claimed that the alderman did not have authority to sentence him.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the Pennsylvania Act of May 1, 1861, P.L. 682 gave the alderman, whose powers were the same as a justice of the peace, authority to impose the sentence. The Act of 1861 granted jurisdiction to justices of the peace to hear and determine certain offenses defined in the Act of March 31, 1860, P.L. 382. On appeal, the prisoner contended that even if the alderman did have jurisdiction to sentence him, the maximum penalty that could be imposed was one year under the Act of 1860. In reversing, the court held that the Act of 1860 was repealed by § 1201 of the Penal Code of June 24, 1939, P.L. 872, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 5201. In all instances, the penalties for the offenses traced from the Act of 1860 to The Penal Code of 1939 were changed. Because the Act of 1861 was a penal provision, the court had to strictly construe it. Thus, the court found that when the legislature passed the Penal Code of 1939 and repealed the Act of 1860, it did not intend that the justices of the peace should have jurisdiction to sentence for violations of the provisions of the Code. Thus, the alderman could not apply the two-year sentence set forth in the Penal Code of 1939.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and discharged the prisoner.

 

667 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cano


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


182 Pa. Super. 524; 128 A.2d 358; 1956 Pa. Super. LEXIS 427


Argued November 17, 1956  
December 28, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 52 and 53, Oct. T., 1957, from judgments of sentence of Court of Quarter Sessions of Schuylkill County, Sept. T., 1953, No. 553, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Aurelio Cano et al. Judgments affirmed.

Proceedings upon informations charging violations of the Anthracite Mine Law. Before DALTON, J.

Demurrer sustained as to corporate defendant; verdicts of guilty as to some counts and not guilty as to others; defendants' motion for new trial refused as to all counts, but motion in arrest of judgment sustained on one count; judgments of sentence entered on remaining counts. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence are affirmed, and the record is remitted to the court below, and it is ordered that defendants appear in the court below at such time as they may there be called, and that they be by that court committed until they have complied with the sentences, or any parts thereof which have not been performed at the time each appeal was made a supersedeas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments of sentence of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Schuylkill County (Pennsylvania), which convicted them on informations charging violations of the Anthracite Mine Law, P.L. 176 (1891), as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 52, § 71 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested on a warrant issued as a result of an affidavit filed by an anthracite mine inspector pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 52, § 511, charging them with being negligently guilty. The prosecution arose out of an occurrence in defendants' mine in which five miners lost their lives. There was no presentment to or indictment by the grand jury as the procedure in the statute provided otherwise. Defendants contended that the absence of a bill of indictment by the grand jury rendered the statutory procedure invalid under Pa. Const. art. I, § 10, and U.S. Const. amend. V. Defendants argued that the offenses charged were indictable offenses that could have been punished at common law. Defendants asserted that the test for determining which offenses were indictable as common law offenses was whether the offenses might have been punished at common law. The court disagreed that the charges against them, in the absence of the statute, would have been indictable as common law offenses. Except as such conduct had been prohibited by statute, the conduct with which defendants were charged did not offend against the public peace, morals, or domestic order of the Commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of sentence. The record was remitted to the court below. Defendants were ordered to appear in the court below at such time as they would be called and were ordered to be committed until they had complied with the sentences or any parts thereof which had not been performed at the time each appeal was made a supersedeas.

 

668 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Pittsburgh v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


182 Pa. Super. 551; 128 A.2d 372; 1956 Pa. Super. LEXIS 428


Argued October 2, 1956  
December 28, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals, Nos. 57, 58, and 64 to 103, inclusive, April T., 1956, from orders of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, dated January 3, 1956, at Complaint Dockets Nos. 16264 et al., in case of City of Pittsburgh v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission et al. Order of commission, to extent indicated, set aside, and record remanded; in other respects, order affirmed.

Proceedings before Public Utility Commission, upon complaints against proposed new tariffs of utility company, and investigation by commission, on its own motion, to determine reasonableness and lawfulness of proposed rates and charges as well as the then existing rates and charges.

Order entered by commission granting specified increase in revenues of utility company. City of Pittsburgh, utility company, and consumer, respectively, appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the commission of January 3, 1956, is, to the extent indicated, set aside, and the record is remanded to the commission for the making of an order (1) requiring The Manufacturers Light and Heat Company to file a tariff with rate schedules designed to produce a return not in excess of 6.30 per cent, (2) modifying the allowance for income taxes to correspond [***2] to the allowable return at the rate of 6.30 per cent, and (3) directing refunds to customers of the excessive amounts collected by The Manufacturers Light and Heat Company under the tariff and schedule filed on January 20, 1956. In other respects the order of the commission is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city, a utility company, and a consumer, all appealed in consolidated cases from orders of appellee, the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, which granted a specified increase in revenues of the utility company.


OVERVIEW: The proceedings began on complaints filed against the utility company's proposed new tariffs and an investigation by the Commission, on its own motion, to determine the reasonableness and lawfulness of proposed and existing rates and charges. On the issue of accrued depreciation and depletion, the court rejected the city's contention that the Commission was bound to accept the book reserve. The city next attacked the Commission's annualization and adjustment of revenues and expenses for test year customer changes. The court determined that the Commission had a wide area of discretion. The court found no error in the Commission's determination of the incremental expense necessary to serve the customer. The court concluded that the evidence sustained the general method used in designing the rate structure. The court found, however, that the utility company was not permitted to pass along the expenses of its parent corporation to the customers. The court held that sums in excess of a fair return on the utility's fair value that the customers of the utility were required to contribute toward the operating expenses of the parent corporation were without justification.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order of the Commission, to the extent indicated, and remanded for an order requiring the company to file a tariff with rate schedules designed to produce a return not in excess of 6.30 percent, modifying the allowance for income taxes to correspond to the allowable return at that rate, and directing refunds to customers of the excessive amounts collected. In other respects, the order of the Commission was affirmed.

 

669 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Goodwin v. County of Allegheny


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


182 Pa. Super. 28; 125 A.2d 640; 1956 Pa. Super. LEXIS 347


Argued July 17, 1956  
October 2, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 171, April T., 1956, from judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, April T., 1956, No. 1316, in case of Bernard H. Goodwin v. County of Allegheny. Judgment reversed.

Case stated in assumpsit.

Judgment entered for plaintiff and against defendant, before ELLENBOGEN, SOFFEL, and LEWIS, JJ., opinion by ELLENBOGEN, J. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is reversed, and here entered for defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Allegheny County sought review from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff Register of Wills and Clerk of the Orphans' Court of Allegheny County, in an action stated in assumpsit.


OVERVIEW: The Register was elected to his office for a four year term to begin in January, 1956. The Act of December 22, 1955, P. L. 788, No. 278, amended the Second Class County Code, § 1810, Act of July 28, 1953, P. L. 723, art. XVIII, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 16, § 2151-1810, and provided for an increase in the annual salary of the Register of Wills and Clerk of the Orphans' Court of Allegheny County of $ 1,000. The Register sought payment from the County for the increase in salary for the month of January, 1956. The lower court held that Pa. Const. art. III, § 13, which prohibited the increase or decrease in salary of public officers after their election or appointment, was not applicable, and therefore, the Register was entitled to the increased salary. On review, the court reversed judgment and held that the prohibition in Pa. Const. art. III, § 13 was applicable to those persons who had been elected to offices which were occupied by public officers, and that it became effective immediately after the election. Therefore, the effect of the Act was to increase the Register's compensation after his election, and this was prohibited by the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment.

 

670 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Obradovich


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


180 Pa. Super. 383; 119 A.2d 839; 1956 Pa. Super. LEXIS 580


Argued September 28, 1955  
January 17, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 169, April T., 1955, from order of County Court of Allegheny County, 1955, No. C-343, in re appeal of Louis Obradovich from decision of Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board. Order affirmed.

Appeal by applicant from decision of Liquor Control Board refusing transfer of liquor license. Before KAUFMAN, J.

Order entered dismissing appeal; exceptions to order dismissed and final order entered, before LENCHER, P.J., BROWN and KAUFMAN, JJ., opinion by KAUFMAN, J. Applicant appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the lower court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of an order of the County Court of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his appeal from a decision by appellee Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board refusing to transfer a restaurant-liquor license to him. When the applicant sought transfer of the license, appellee protestants objected to the transfer.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought to have a restaurant-liquor license transferred to him for certain premises. His application was opposed by the protestants, who resided in the vicinity of those premises. The Board refused his application. The lower court issued an order dismissing his appeal from that refusal. Upon further appeal, the court affirmed that order. The court noted that the premises at issue were located in a neighborhood that was almost completely residential. It further noted that the lower court found that the premises were situated at the end of block of business establishments. Further, the court remarked that children continuously passed the premises on their way to a school and a park. The court concluded that the Board did not abuse its discretion in refusing the application for the transfer. The court rejected the applicant's argument that because the premises themselves were zoned commercial, the Board could not refuse the transfer on the ground that the neighborhood itself was residential in character. The court commented that a municipality could not, in the guise of a zoning ordinance, regulate the business of dispensing liquor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court, which dismissed the applicant's appeal from the Board's decision.

 

671 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Root v. Erie Zoning Board of Appeals


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


180 Pa. Super. 38; 118 A.2d 297; 1955 Pa. Super. LEXIS 568


Argued October 3, 1955  
November 17, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 33, April T., 1955, from order of Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Sept. T., 1954, No. 106, in case of J. A. Root v. City of Erie Zoning Board of Appeals. Order affirmed.

Appeal by applicant from decision of zoning board refusing building permit. Before EVANS, P.J.

Order entered directing permit to issue and sustaining appeal; exceptions to order dismissed and final order entered. Zoning board appealed.



DISPOSITION: The order of the lower court is affirmed at the cost of the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant zoning board challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), which directed the zoning board to issue a building permit to appellee applicant. The applicant's petition for a building permit had been denied. The property in question was located in a commercial district.


OVERVIEW: The zoning ordinance provided that the building line of any structure or alterations to an existing structure had to have been set back at least 10 feet from the street line. The permit authorized would permit the alteration of the building so as to add to the front thereof a well designed and artistic business front within the 10 foot setback space. The testimony revealed that approximately half of the buildings on the block were, and had been since the passage of the zoning ordinance, built out to the street line. The court rejected the zoning board's contention that the applicant had to prove hardship. The court reasoned that an applicant for a special exception did not need to carry the burden of proving unnecessary hardship. It was when seeking a variance that the applicant therefor had to show that unnecessary hardship would result unless the variance was permitted. The court held that to require the applicant to observe the setback provisions of the zoning ordinance when the properties of many other owners failed to comply would have been most unfair and the zoning board's action in requiring strict compliance should have been characterized as unreasonable and arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with costs to the zoning board.

 

672 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Bozzi


THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


178 Pa. Super. 224; 116 A.2d 290; 1955 Pa. Super. LEXIS 487


Argued March 21, 1955.  
July 21, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 127, Oct. T., 1955, from judgment of Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County, April T., 1954, No. 970, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. James Bozzi. Judgment affirmed.

Indictment charging defendant with unlawful possession of narcotics. Before DAVIS, J.

Verdict of guilty and judgment of sentence thereon. Defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Quarter Sessions of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which entered his conviction for unlawful possession of narcotics.


OVERVIEW: None of the grand jurors resided in defendant's ward. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in not quashing the indictment on the ground that he was not afforded the right to examine the jury commissioners as to the method of selecting jurors. The court rejected such contention because the provisions of the Act of May 10, 1949, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 17, § 1251, afforded no such right to defendant. Defendant also argued that the charge was improper because the trial court failed to define "possession." The court also rejected that argument because the word "possession" had a common meaning that was generally understood and the charge fully covered the essentials of the offense. Moreover, because the question was not included in the motions for a new trial and in arrest of judgment, it was not properly raised for the first time on appeal. Finally, the court ruled that § 12 of the Act of July 11, 1917, as amended by Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 865, under which sentence was imposed, was not an unconstitutional invasion of the powers of the judiciary by the legislature. The legislature was authorized to prescribe the punishment to be meted out for violations of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

673 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Di Meglio


The Superior Court of Pennsylvania


179 Pa. Super. 472; 117 A.2d 767; 1955 Pa. Super. LEXIS 657


Argued March 29, 1955  
July 21, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals Nos. 80 and 81, Oct. T., 1954, from judgments of Court of Quarter Sessions of Delaware County, June T., 1952, No. 6, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Frank DiMeglio and Nick DiMeglio. Judgments affirmed; reargument refused September 6, 1955.

Appeals by defendants from summary conviction before justice of the peace for violation of the General Food Law. Before TOAL, J.

Verdicts of guilty and judgments of sentence thereon. Defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgments of Court of Quarter Sessions of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which convicted them upon a hearing de novo following defendants' prior convictions for violations of the Pennsylvania General Food Law, Act of May 13, 1909, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 31, § 1, et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were proprietors of a restaurant who sold lemon pies made from Jell-O Brand lemon filling. Because the pies were adulterated with yellow coal tar color, defendants were charged with a violation of the General Food Law. Following defendants' convictions before a justice of the peace, a court of quarter sessions held a hearing de novo, found them guilty, and ordered them to pay a fine and costs. On further appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendants clearly violated §§ 3 and 8 of the General Food Law and Regulation 1003 of the Pennsylvania Department because they sold pies adulterated with artificial coloring. Based on testimony from the Commonwealth's expert baker witness, there was sufficient evidence to find that the purpose of the dye was to conceal inferiority in quality. Although defendants used a product that had been legally shipped into the state, the addition of eggs, water and pie crust made it a new product that caused the Jell-O filling to lose its interstate characteristic and become entirely intrastate in every respect. Because control of foodstuff was within the Commonwealth's police power, defendants' convictions were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

Commonwealth ex rel. Lyons v. Day


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


177 Pa. Super. 392; 110 A.2d 871; 1955 Pa. Super. LEXIS 756


November 16, 1954, Argued  
January 14, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 36, Oct. T., 1955, from order of Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County, June T., 1954, No. 1699, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania ex rel. Abraham Lyons v. Charles G. Day, Warden.

Habeas corpus. Before Levinthal, J.

Order entered granting writ and discharging relator. Respondent appealed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent warden appealed from the order of the Court of Common Pleas No. 1 of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), granting petitioner relator a writ of habeas corpus and discharging him from custody. The issue was whether the amending Act of July 29, 1953, P.L. 1447, § 1 (1953 amendment), enacted after the relator was sentenced, and which limited a general sentence to the state reformatory to six years, applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: The relator was originally given a general sentence on a burglary conviction to the Pennsylvania Industrial School, the state reformatory, under the Act of April 28, 1887, P.L. 63, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 485. During his incarceration, he was paroled, recommitted, reparoled, and recommitted. Seven years after his original sentence, he was transferred to the state prison, to serve the remainder of his 20-year maximum sentence. That same year, the 1887 statute was amended by the Act of July 29, 1953, P.L. 1447, § 1. The amendment provided for a maximum general sentence to the reformatory of six years. The relator argued that the amendment should be applied retroactively and that he should therefore be discharged. The court found that the relator, by his parole violations, had demonstrated his lack of fitness to return to society. The court also found that he had never applied for parole. It held that habeas corpus was not a substitute for parole. It also held unanimously that, based on principals of statutory construction and the public interest, the legislature had not intended the amendment to apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was dismissed. The relator was remanded to the custody of the warden. The court held that the amending statute was not meant to apply retroactively.

Santus Unemployment Comp. Case


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


177 Pa. Super. 496; 110 A.2d 874; 1955 Pa. Super. LEXIS 773


November 10, 1954, Argued  
January 14, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, No. 200, April T., 1954, by claimant, from decision of Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, appeal No. B-4-H-443, decision No. B-36397, in re claim of John P. Santus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision from the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, which denied the employee's application for unemployment compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an appeal from a decision of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review denying certain unemployment benefits. The record showed that the employee was laid off due to lack of work, and about a month before the lay off, the employee was granted one week of vacation and was paid for two other weeks for which he was entitled. The Board disallowed benefits for one week upon the basis of a regulation which provided that vacation paid to an employee was to be allocated to the first period of otherwise compensable unemployment occurring within 90 days following such payment. The court affirmed the Board's decision and concluded that the Department of Unemployment Compensation had the power to determine by the appropriate regulations the periods for which vacation pay should be deemed remuneration. The court held that the regulation, adopted under § 4(u) of the Unemployment Compensation Law, was not arbitrary or discriminatory, and it was not an unconstitutional delegation of the legislative power. The court ruled that the Law was not intended to create a situation whereby an employee could receive both vacation pay and unemployment compensation for the same period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, denying the employee's application for unemployment compensation benefits.
