Hilltown Township v. Horn


Nos. 966 and 978 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


13 Pa. Commw. 248; 320 A.2d 153; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 925


April 2, 1974, Argued  
June 6, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County in case of In Re: Appeal of Vernon Horn and Edith Horn, his wife, from the Hilltown Township Zoning Hearing Board, No. 72-1341-05-6 March Term, 1971.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania) reversing the Zoning Hearing Board's (Board) order that prohibited the operation of a quarry and the use of a farmhouse on the property as an office and appellee property owners sought review of the part of the Board's determination that operation of an asphalt plant on appellees' property was in violation of the zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owners requested permits for the operation and expansion of their quarry, a new blacktop plant, and an office building. The Zoning Hearing Board (Board) affirmed a zoning officer's decision refusing the permits for the operation of the quarry, blacktop plant, and office. The court affirmed the lower court's decision reversing the Board's order that prohibited the operation of the quarry and the use of a farmhouse on the property as an office and affirmed the Board's determination that the operation of an asphalt plant on appellants' premises was in violation of a zoning ordinance. The court concluded that there was insufficient evidence on the record to support the Board's finding of abandonment of the nonconforming quarry operation. Testimony from workers showed that appellants had kept the quarry operational so as to retain its nonconforming use and evidence was sufficient to support the fact that the house was used as an office for the quarry and its use was a nonconforming one as part of the totality of the quarry operation. The court held that appellants could not expand the allowable quarrying nonconforming use to a second nonconforming use, an asphalt plant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order reversing the Zoning Hearing Board's (Board) decision that prohibited the operation of a quarry and use of a farmhouse as an office on appellee owner's land and affirmed the Board's determination that operation of an asphalt plant violated the zoning ordinance. The court found that there was insufficient evidence to support the Board's finding of abandonment of the nonconforming quarry operation.

Appellee's decision was supported by substantial evidence.

South Union Township Sewage Authority v. Kozares


No. 1139 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


13 Pa. Commw. 325; 320 A.2d 381; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 940


January 9, 1974, Argued  
May 30, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County in case of Victor Kozares, Harry B. Moats, Ewing Newcomer, Michael Janosick, Earl George, James E. Hayden, Dennis Cropp, Frank Lechnar, Fred Matelli, William Morganosky, Wendell Goodwin, Lloyd Hunter, Carl Petno and John Cipoletti v. South Union Township Sewage Authority and Township of South Union, No. 2737 in Equity.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality and sewage authority sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County (Pennsylvania) dismissing exceptions filed by appellants to a decree nisi enjoining them from making or enforcing a front-foot sewer assessment, and further ordering appellant sewage authority to submit a revised sewer assessment schedule for further review by the court.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, individuals on behalf of all the residents of appellant municipality, filed a petition for preliminary injunction alleging that a sewage tap-in fee, front-foot assessment, and monthly service fees were excessive and unreasonable, and prayed that appellant municipality and sewage authority be enjoined from collecting these fees, and that the ordinance enforcing payment of such fees be set aside as unconstitutional. The court reversed the lower court's preliminary injunction restraining appellants from enforcing the ordinance requiring property owners to tap into the sewer system or be subject to fines, and reversed the lower court's decree nisi concluding that as a matter of law, the front-foot assessment was unreasonable and inequitable as it applied to substandard housing and vacant lots. The court held that rate-making was the exclusive function of the authority under 53 P.S. § 306B(h), and the lower court's duty was to determine the uniformity and reasonableness of the rate, not whether it would choose a different method of establishing reasonable and uniform rates. The court found appellees had failed to show the authority had abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decree enjoining appellant municipality and sewage authority from making or enforcing a front-foot sewer assessment and order to appellant sewer authority to submit a revised sewer assessment. The court held that the lower court sitting in equity did not have the jurisdiction to determine the reasonableness of the rates established by appellants and there was not showing of abuse of discretion.

Dussia v. Barger


No. 1099 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


13 Pa. Commw. 571; 319 A.2d 685; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 983


February 6, 1974, Argued  
May 24, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Lieutenant Colonel Joseph Dussia v. Colonel James D. Barger, Commissioner of the Pennsylvania State Police, and Major Sidney C. Deyo, Captain Earl O. Bergstrom and Captain Stanley B. Kramer, Members of the Court-Martial Board.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for defendants. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer and defendants, state police commissioner and court-martial board members, requested findings of fact and conclusions of law in plaintiff's action in equity that sought a decree to enjoin defendants from convening and conducting a court-martial.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff police officer sought to enjoin defendants, state police commissioner and court-martial board members, from conducting a court-martial against him. The parties requested findings of fact and conclusions of law, and the court entered judgment in favor of defendants. The court reaffirmed its holding that the court martial statute, Administrative Code § 711, 71 P.S. § 251, and its related regulations were constitutional, and rejected as irrelevant plaintiff's contention that he was improperly suspended without a prior hearing. In deciding whether defendant commissioner had expressed in a conversation with plaintiff, that plaintiff was guilty, the court credited defendant commissioner's version of the conversation; defendant commissioner's statements only apprised the plaintiff that there was evidence against him and suggested that resignation should be considered, a common practice known to plaintiff. Defendant commissioner's rules would allow plaintiff to challenge allegedly prejudiced defendant board members, and disqualifying from the board all members subordinate to plaintiff would disqualify every member of the force except defendant commissioner.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of defendants, state police commissioner and court-martial board members, in plaintiff police officer's complaint to enjoin a court martial against him, because the court martial statute and regulations were constitutional, the court credited defendant commissioner's testimony that he had not pre-judged plaintiff's guilt, and plaintiff could challenge defendant board members for prejudice at the court-martial.

Purolator Courier Corp. v. Commonwealth, Public Utility Com.


No. 688 C.D. 1971


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


13 Pa. Commw. 444; 319 A.2d 688; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 961


February 6, 1974, Argued  
May 17, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission in case of Application of James C. Wetherill, t/d/b/a Hatboro Delivery Service, No. A-78703, F.1, Am-G.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted. Appeal quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant courier services sought review of an order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Intervening appellee courier service filed a motion to quash the appeal as untimely under § 502 of the Appellate Court Jurisdiction Act of 1970, 17 P.S. § 211.502. Appellants contended that the time limitations under § 1101 of the Public Utility Law, 66 P.S. § 1431, were controlling.


OVERVIEW: Intervening appellee courier service filed a motion to quash an appeal filed by appellant courier services from an order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Appellee contended that the appeal was untimely under § 502 of the Appellate Court Jurisdiction Act of 1970 (ACJA), 17 P.S. § 211.502, because it was not filed within 30 days of the entry of the order. Appellants contended that § 1101 of the Public Utility Law, 66 P.S. § 1431, provided the time limitation for the appeal. Under § 1101, appellants were required to bring an appeal within 30 days after the service of the commission's order. There was no dispute that the appeal would be timely under the Public Utility Law but not under the ACJA. The court granted the motion to quash. The court held that the two provisions were clearly in conflict and that the general repealer provision of § 509(f) of the ACJA, 17 P.S. § 211.509(f), controlled. The court held that § 509(f) repealed the provisions of the Public Utility Law that were inconsistent with the ACJA.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to quash filed by intervening appellee courier service. The court held that appellant courier services did not take an appeal from an order of the Public Utility Commission within the time provided by the Appellate Court Jurisdiction Act. The court held that an inconsistent time limitation provided in the Public Utility Law had been repealed.

Sobocinski v. Williamsport


No. 358 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


13 Pa. Commw. 425; 319 A.2d 697; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 958


December 6, 1973, Argued  
May 14, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County in case of City of Williamsport v. Joseph Sobocinski, Criminal No. 72-10, 807.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which found him guilty of violating a weed ordinance, Williamsport, Pa., Ordinance 2765 art. 721 (May 7, 1959), and fined him after he failed to cut the grass at a property owned by him.


OVERVIEW: Appellant resident violated Williamsport, Pa., Ordinance 2765 art. 721 (May 7, 1959) when he failed to cut the grass at his property located in appellant city. Appellant contended that the weed ordinance was facially unconstitutional because it was an invalid exercise of the police power, it denied him due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because it was vague and did not provide for preabatement hearings, and the fines were in violation of Pa. Const. art. I, § 13. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The nuisance ordinance was a reasonable exercise of police power because weeds allowed to grow to excess affected the public health by producing allergenic pollen noxious odors. Substantive and procedural due process were satisfied because the taking of uncultivated weeds and grass was not a significant property interest. The common meaning of the words "grass" and "weeds" gave appellant an adequate standard by which to gauge his conduct. The fines were reasonable, and the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant resident for his failure to abide by appellee city's weed ordinance. Appellant created a nuisance when he failed to cut grass at his property, and the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of police power in responding to the nuisance. There was no taking of any significant property interest. The ordinance was clear as to what standard by which appellant should have gauged his conduct.

Upper St. Clair Township v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Community Affairs


No. 1090 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


13 Pa. Commw. 71; 317 A.2d 906; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 896


January 7, 1974, Argued  
April 5, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Department of Community Affairs in case of In Re: Application of the Township of Upper St. Clair for Project 500 development funds, Order of July 23, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained. Order set aside. Record remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of the adjudication of appellee Department of Community Affairs (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's application for development funds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant township applied for funds for a park project to appellee Department of Community Affairs under the Land and Water Conservation and Reclamation Act, 32 P.S. § 5101 et seq. Appellee's secretary denied the application. Appellant made exception to the denial, and following an evidentiary hearing under the §§ 31 through 33 of the Administrative Agency Law, 71 P.S. §§ 1710.31 - 1710.33, appellee's secretary adopted a panel's report and again denied the application. The court sustained the appeal, set aside appellee's order, and remanded with directions that appellee approve appellant's application. The court held that appellee had abused its power. The court held that appellant had not shown any authority for the denial to an otherwise-qualified municipality of state funds based upon the assertion that appellant's land development policies excluded the poor and minorities. The court held that the record did not support a finding that appellant's conditions of being predominately populated with white people of better-than-average income and containing valuable land and improvements were the result of zoning restrictions rather than other causes.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the appeal, set aside appellee Department of Community Affairs' order, and remanded with directions that appellee approve appellant township's application for development funds under the Land and Water Conservation and Reclamation Act, because the denial was an abuse of power and appellant had not shown any authority for the denial to an otherwise-qualified municipality of state funds.

 

769 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Boyd v. Commonwealth, State Board of Osteopathic Examiners


No. 658 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


12 Pa. Commw. 620; 317 A.2d 307; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1108


December 4, 1973, Argued  
March 27, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Board of Osteopathic Examiners, in case of In the Matter of the Suspension or Revocation of the License to Practice Osteopathy and Surgery Issued to Nathaniel W. Boyd, D.O., dated April 11, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of the order of appellee State Board of Osteopathic Examiners (Pennsylvania), which suspended his license to engage in the practice of osteopathy and surgery for six months based on his alleged violation of 63 P.S. § 271 and 49 Pa. Code § 25.61 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellee State Board of Osteopathic Examiners suspended the license issued to appellant physician to engage in the practice of osteopathy and surgery based on appellant's alleged violations of 63 P.S. § 271, and 49 Pa. Code § 25.61 et seq. Appellee based its conclusion on findings of fact which indicated that appellant advertised his services through direct mail and in the newspaper. On appeal, the court affirmed appellee's adjudication. The court held that the facts established that appellant violated the regulations of his profession concerning unethical advertising. Appellee did not act in an arbitrary or capricious manner in refusing to address appellant's charge that it was prejudicially composed given the fact that no judicial officer had a direct, personal or substantial pecuniary interest in the outcome of the controversy. A clerical error mislabeling two of the medical doctors as "O.D.'s" on a list of board members did not change the fact that the composition of the board met all legal requirements. The six-month suspension was not an abuse of discretion and the advertising regulations were valid as an exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication of appellee State Board of Osteopathic Examiners suspending appellant physician's license to engage in the practice of osteopathy and surgery for six months because the facts established that appellant violated the regulations of his profession concerning unethical advertising, the penalty was not an abuse of discretion, and the advertising regulations were valid as an exercise of the state's police power.

 

770 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Percival v. Philadelphia


Nos. 1062 to 1073 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


12 Pa. Commw. 628; 317 A.2d 667; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1109


June 6, 1973, Argued  
March 21, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of City of Philadelphia v. Raymond F. Percival, No. 9-229; Abner B. Deckert, No. 9-228; Timothy J. Eastburn, No. 9-227; Michael J. Nole, No. 9-226; William A. MacDonald, No. 9-225; Guy W. Harvey, Jr., No. 9-224; Leslie Stevenson, Jr., No. 9-223; William E. Gould, No. 9-222; Nicholas Buompastore, No. 9-221; William H. Hazzard, No. 9-220; Thomas P. Jenkins, No. 9-219; B. R. Covert, No. 9-218; Joseph F. Kenney, No. 9-217; E. A. Thomas, No. 2-216, September Sessions, 1972.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city nonresidents sought review of orders of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which declared absolute rules upon them to show cause why writs of capias ad respondendum should not issue to collect unpaid taxes to appellee City of Philadelphia on their earned income, and which set bail.


OVERVIEW: Appellants city nonresidents were employed within the city, and refused to file returns of or pay appellee City of Philadelphia's tax on earned income. Appellee initiated proceedings under statutes that authorized the use of capias ad respondendum to collect the taxes owed. The trial court issued orders against each appellant that declared an absolute rule to show cause why a writ of capias ad respondendum should not issue and set bail. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court was empowered to adopt its rule related to capias ad respondendum. The court held that the local court rule and hearings conducted by the trial court offered appellants due process incident to the allowance of the issuance of writs of capias ad respondendum. The court held that the bail set by the trial court, based upon the number of apparent offenses and the possible fines, was not excessive and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII guarantees. The court held that appellants' rights to equal protection were not violated by the exemption of married women under 12 P.S. § 304. The court held that the exemption of married women provided by 12 P.S. § 304 offended Pa. Const. art. I, § 28.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders declaring absolute rules upon appellant city nonresidents to show cause why writs of capias ad respondendum should not issue, because the trial court was empowered to adopt a rule related to capias ad respondendum, the local court rule and the trial court's hearings offered appellants due process, and the bail set was not excessive and did not violate Eighth Amendment guarantees.

 

771 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Koynok v. Commonwealth, State Bd. of Private Academic Schools


No. 689 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


12 Pa. Commw. 375; 316 A.2d 118; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1068


December 4, 1973, Argued  
March 11, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of George L. Koynok and Mary C. Koynok, t/d/b/a Glenmore Academy v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, State Board of Private Academic Schools, Dr. L. Wagenhorst, President, and N. Eugene Shoemaker, Secretary of the Board.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State Board of Private Academic Schools (board), its president and secretary, filed preliminary objections to the complaint filed by plaintiff private school owners seeking damages and injunctive relief, which alleged that plaintiffs had been injured as a result of an evaluation conducted by defendant board on their private school.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff private school owners filed a complaint against defendants, the State Board of Private Academic Schools (board), its president and secretary, seeking damages and injunctive relief based on defendant board's evaluation of the school. Defendants filed preliminary objections, which the court granted. The court found that plaintiffs' action for money damages against defendants was barred by Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, which provided that suits could be brought against the commonwealth only where the legislature directed, and that immunity extended to instrumentalities of the commonwealth engaged in governmental functions. The court determined that plaintiffs' action against defendants president and secretary was also barred by the doctrine, because sovereign immunity extended to high public officials acting officially within the scope of their authority with respect to official communications and acts. The court held that plaintiffs' request for injunctive relief was barred because in actions involving immunity, injunctive relief was granted only to restrain the commonwealth from enforcing provisions of a statute claimed to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the preliminary objections of defendants, the State Board of Private Academic Schools, its president and secretary, to the complaint filed by plaintiff private school owners, because defendants were immune from suit under the doctrine of sovereign immunity.

 

772 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Sweet v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board


No. 17 Tr. Dkt. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


12 Pa. Commw. 358; 316 A.2d 665; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1066; 85 L.R.R.M. 2753


November 7, 1973, Argued  
March 5, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board in case of In the Matter of the Employees of Washington County, No. PERA-R-2209-W. Transferred to the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania from the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania, September 10, 1973.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judges challenged the decision of appellee Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, which found that a county, acting through its commissioners, was the public employer of court-related employees of that county within the meaning of the Public Employee Relations Act, 43 P.S. § 1101.101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board issued a final order, which included a determination that a county, acting through its commissioners, was the public employer of the court-related employees of that county as defined under the Public Employee Relations Act (Act), 43 P.S. § 1101.101 et seq. Appellant judges challenged this determination and argued that they or the court itself were the public employer of such employees. The court disagreed and affirmed the order. Under the Act, 43 P.S. § 1101.301, the court found that the county was a public employer as it was considered a "political subdivision" within the Act's definition of a public employer, and that court-related employees were considered public employees thereunder as well. The court held that the Act as it applied to court-related personnel did not interfere with the proper function of the courts or the administration of justice to constitute a legislative encroachment upon the judicial branch of the state government. The court found, therefore, that the Act did not violate Pa. Const. art. V, § 1 which established a unified judicial system as a separate and independent branch.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of appellee labor relations board, which held that a county, not appellant judges, was the public employer of the court-related employees of that county. The court reasoned that the county was considered a "political subdivision" within the public employer definition in the Public Employees Relations Act, that court-related employees were public employees, and that the Act did not violate separation of powers.

 

773 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. South Centre Township Supervisors


No. 739 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


12 Pa. Commw. 285; 315 A.2d 379; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1054


December 4, 1973, Argued  
February 14, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Columbia County in case of In Re: Appeal of R. G. Smith from Report and Decision of South Centre Township Supervisors concerning Application for Zoning Change, No. 441 October Term, 1971.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Columbia County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's challenge from appellee board of supervisor's decision to refuse appellant's petition to rezone his property from interchange or beautification to general commercial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner purchased land that adjoined a major highway and was used for automobile and truck repairs. The township enacted a zoning ordinance which zoned appellant's land as interchange or beautification and allowed the land to be used only for growing grasses, flowers, and shrubbery. After appellant's petition for a variance was finally granted, appellant filed a petition to change the zoning of his property to general commercial. When appellee board of supervisors denied the application and the trial court affirmed, appellant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed and found that the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code (MPC), 53 P.S. § 10101 et seq. did not provide that a landowner could appeal from the rezoning of an area in which his land was located. The court found that the validity or constitutionality of an enactment would not be decided until the enactment was actually applied. The court found that the MPC only provided a right to appeal from decisions of the zoning hearing board. The court found that appellant did not follow the proper procedures which would permit the court to rule on the zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court below, which denied appellant property owner's challenge of appellee board of supervisor's decision to refuse appellant's petition to rezone land. The court affirmed because appellant did not follow proper procedures that would have allowed the court to examine the validity of the zoning ordinance.

 

774 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Manoa Shopping Center, Inc. v. Zoning Hearing Board


No. 230 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


11 Pa. Commw. 569; 314 A.2d 516; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1148


October 5, 1973, Argued  
January 17, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, in case of In Re: Application of Mid Island Properties and/or Manoa Shopping Center, No. 6395 of 1972.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant shopping center challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania) which affirmed the decision of appellee zoning board upholding the denial of a building permit to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant shopping center sought to enlarge its facility by constructing a new retail store located separately at the northern edge of its property. It applied for a permit, which was denied by the building inspector, and this denial was upheld by appellee zoning board (Board). The trial court, which took no additional evidence on appeal, affirmed the Board. The issue on appeal was the number of parking spaces that appellant had to provide for the new store as required by Haverford Township, Pa., Ordinance 1326 (Dec. 11, 1967). The shopping center contended that the existing spaces were legally sufficient for the entire shopping center, even with the addition of the new store. After review, this court concluded that Ordinance 1326 was applicable to the entire shopping center, and that appellant had to provide additional spaces for the new store. It could not be permitted to reduce its current parking facilities by attributing some of those spaces to the new store. The building inspector acted correctly by refusing to grant the building permit. The lower court's order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court which affirmed the decision of appellee zoning board to uphold the denial of a building permit to appellant shopping center was affirmed because appellant failed to prove that the questioned ordinance was confiscatory, arbitrary, or unreasonable.

 

775 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Wm. Penn Parking Garage, Inc. v. Pittsburgh


No. 525 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


11 Pa. Commw. 507; 314 A.2d 322; 1974 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1135


November 7, 1973, Argued  
January 16, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of W. Penn Parking Garage, Inc.; Alco Parking Corporation; Campus Parking, Inc.; Fourth Avenue Parking, Inc.; Grant Parking, Inc.; Harry W. Sheppard, Jr., t/a Stanwix Auto Park; John Stabile and John Stabile, Jr., t/a Wm. Penn Parking Lot; Meyers Bros. Parking-Central Corp.; Parking Service Corporation, Inc., et al., v. City of Pittsburgh, No. S.A. 106 of 1973.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parking lot operators and appellants individuals sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) sustaining appellee city's demurrer and dismissing appellants' petition, which challenged appellee city's ordinance which imposed a 20 percent tax on each parking transaction, without evidentiary hearing or leave to amend.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city approved an ordinance which imposed upon each parking transaction, by a patron of a nonresidential parking place, a tax of 20 percent on the consideration for each transaction. Appellants challenged the ordinance pursuant to the Local Tax Enabling Act (Act), Pa. Stat. tit. 53, § 6906. Appellee city filed preliminary objections which included a demurrer on the ground that the complaint relied on an unconstitutional delegation of taxing power to the judiciary. The lower court sustained the demurrer and dismissed appellants' petition. The court reversed the lower court's ruling. The lower court ruled that appellants lacked standing. The court disagreed and found that appellants, both parking lot operators and individuals, had standing to challenge the tax under the Act. Further, the court found that the Act was constitutional and did not improperly delegate legislative power to the judiciary. The power to invalidate a taxing measure in whole or in part was not the power to tax, as asserted by the lower court. Also, the power to reduce the rates of taxes, did not, in the court's view, confer upon the court the power to tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order dismissing appellants parking lot operators' and appellant individuals' petition without evidentiary hearing or leave to amend because the court found that appellants had standing to file the petition and the lower court had improperly ruled that the relevant statute was unconstitutional.

Bucks County Bd. of Comm'Rs v. Commonwealth


Nos. 298 C.D. 1973, 783 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


11 Pa. Commw. 487; 313 A.2d 185; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 490; 2 P.U.R.4th 396


September 10, 1973, Argued  
December 12, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument as to 298 C.D. 1973, Denied January 8, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Orders of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission in case of Application of Interstate Energy Company, Docket No. A. 97032.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county government bodies, railroad trustees, environmental committees, and environmentalist challenged orders of appellee Public Utility Commission (PUC) that granted a certificate of public convenience to appellee energy company to supply service by pipeline in the transportation of petroleum products. Appellant Pennsylvania Department of Transportation challenged appellee PUC's order that denied a petition for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Public Utility Commission (PUC) granted appellee energy company a certificate of public convenience required for the construction of a pipeline to supply oil to fuel new power plants. Appellant county government bodies, railroad trustees, environmental committees, and environmentalist challenged the order granting the certificate, and an order denying a petition for rehearing. The court affirmed. The court held that appellee PUC's conclusion that a pipeline would be more efficient and less polluting than alternatives proposed by appellants was supported by ample evidence. The court also held that appellee PUC did not abuse its discretion by concluding that negative environmental effects could be minimized by careful construction and line selection, and the implementation of work quality standards. The court affirmed a finding that appellee energy company was a public utility even though it only served a few customers, and that the proposed pipeline construction did not violate Pa. Const. art. 1, § 27. The order denying a rehearing was affirmed because the petition failed to describe any new evidence that had become available to justify a rehearing.


OUTCOME: Appellee Public Utility Commission's order granting a certificate of public convenience to allow appellee energy company to build an oil pipeline, and its order denying rehearing, was affirmed. The findings upon which the order granting the certificate was based had substantial support in the record. The denial of a rehearing was not an abuse of discretion.

Springdale & Wilkins v. Kane


Nos. 341 C.D. 1973, 477 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


11 Pa. Commw. 254; 312 A.2d 611; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 429


September 10, 1973, Argued  
December 4, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in cases of The Townships of Springdale and Wilkins v. Robert P. Kane, Secretary of Revenue, Robert P. Casey, Auditor General, Israel Packel, Attorney General, and Grace M. Sloan, State Treasurer, of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania; and The School Districts of Deer Lakes and Allegheny Valley, The Townships of Springdale, Wilkins and Harmar, The Borough of Cheswick, all political subdivisions of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Robert P. Kane, Secretary of Revenue and Robert P. Casey, Auditor General, and Israel Packel, Attorney General, and Grace M. Sloan, State Treasurer, of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Objections overruled in No. 341 C.D. 1973. Objections sustained and complaint dismissed in No. 477 C.D. 1973.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff townships, brought action against defendant state officials, alleging that defendants collected revenue from the imposition of the Public Utility Realty Tax Act (PURTA), 72 P. S. § 3271, et seq., but that in violation of the constitutional mandate, defendants had failed to pay plaintiffs any portion of the funds due from the PURTA tax for a 9 month period.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff townships sought an order from the court directing defendant state officials, to distribute monies collected under Public Utility Realty Tax Act (PURTA), 72 P. S. § 3271, et seq., for the calendar year 1970 to all local taxing authorities in the Commonwealth, attorney counsel fees, and to make an accounting. The court overruled the preliminary objections of defendant auditor general finding that defendant auditor general obviously had responsibilities in connection with the constitutional mandate and the legislative scheme of distributing PURTA tax dollars. The court also found that defendants did not have sovereign immunity because the action sought to enforce a constitutional mandate. The laches defense failed because there was nothing on the record that would permit the court to rule as a matter of law that defendants had been prejudiced by the delay. The forfeiture provision of 72 P. S. § 3276 was constitutional and because plaintiff school district failed to file the reports required of all local taxing authorities the court held that plaintiff school district had failed to state a cause of action, and the preliminary objections of defendants were sustained.


OUTCOME: All of the preliminary objections of defendant officials were overruled as to plaintiff township, in their action alleging defendants collected revenue from the imposition of a public utility realty tax and failed to distribute the share due plaintiffs for 1970. The court held that the preliminary objections must be overruled because inter alia, defendants were not immune from suit and laches did not apply.

Payne v. Kassab


No. 1061 C.D. 1971


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


11 Pa. Commw. 14; 312 A.2d 86; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 440


September 10, 1973, Argued  
November 21, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Marion Woodward Payne, Sara Wolfe Bell, Lea M. Csala, Frances Phelps Waller, Rachael W. Gutman, Anthony J. Mussari, Barbara B. Albert, Magdalene Dysleski, Stella M. Moat, Elizabeth C. Miner, George Loveland, Esquire, Carolyn H. Reif, Judith L. Reishtein, Anthony J. Walaitis and Stella Walaitis, his wife, and The Wilkes College Students' Committee for a Clean Environment, by Mark Chamberlain, Trustee Ad Litem v. Jacob G. Kassab, Individually and as Secretary of the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation, and The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania Department of Transportation; City of Wilkes-Barre, John B. McGlynn, Mayor, Marjorie Bart, Robert P. Brader, John V. Morris, Kenneth Remensnyder, Con Salwoski and Joseph A. Williams, Councilmen of the City of Wilkes-Barre, Luzerne County, Pennsylvania.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff activists filed an action in equity in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania against defendants, government representatives and city, to enjoin a proposed road widening project that would have encroached on a public common of local historical significance on grounds that the project violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 27 and 71 P.S. § 512(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, government representatives and city, proposed to widen two streets in the city of Wilkes-Barre under a plan that would cause the project to encroach onto a public common of local historical significance. The plan contained provisions that protected the environmental quality of the common. Plaintiff activists filed an equity action pursuant to Pa. Const. art. I, § 27 and 71 P.S. § 512(b) to enjoin the project. The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss. The court held that the proposed project was not unconstitutional and not in violation of § 512(b) because defendants considered all statutorily required effects of the project and made a reasonable effort to reduce environmental incursion, and because plaintiffs could not show that environmental harm clearly outweighed the benefits of the project. The court also held that the project did not violate the original grant of the public common because the common's original features would be retained.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss. The court held that defendants' road-widening project was not constitutionally impermissible because defendants complied with all applicable statutes and made a reasonable effort to reduce environmental incursion, and because plaintiff activists failed to show the environmental harm clearly outweighed the benefits of the project.

Southeastern Pennsylvania Transp. Authority v. Yellow Limousine Service, Inc.


No. 698 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


10 Pa. Commw. 572; 312 A.2d 79; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 576


September 5, 1973, Argued  
November 20, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of In Re: Appeal of Yellow Limousine Service from Adoption by the Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority of Proposed Tariff No. 9 -- Proposed Airport Express Bus Route, No. 4380 December Term, 1969.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee limousine service's petition restraining appellant from instituting a direct bus service from the airport to the city.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority published a tariff under which it proposed to provide a scheduled bus service between the airport and the city. Appellee limousine service, a public utility, opposed the tariff and filed a petition to restrain appellant from instituting the proposed service. The trial court granted appellee's petition, concluding that the parties' services were comparable. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the trial court, holding that the parties' services were not comparable. The court held that 66 P.S. § 2004(d)(9) of the Metropolitan Transportation Authorities Act was not intended to prohibit appellant from providing services to its current customers, but was intended to prohibit those services that were to take appellee's customers. The court concluded that appellant was not competing against appellee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, ruling that the statute was not intended to prohibit appellant Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority from providing transportation services to its current customers, but was only applicable if appellant's purpose was to compete with appellee limousine service. The court held that, although the parties' services were similar, they were not comparable.

Commonwealth by Creamer v. Monumental Properties, Inc.


No. 1241 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


10 Pa. Commw. 596; 314 A.2d 333; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 578


May 8, 1973, Argued  
November 7, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, by J. Shane Creamer, Attorney General, v. Monumental Properties, Inc., Capital Housing Corporation, Executive House, Inc., Property Management, Inc., Samuel Elgart, Inc., Frank Stein, Albert Kaytes, Harry B. Davis, Donald Yost Real Estate Company, Miller Bros. & Company, William B. Hollinger & Son, Benjamin Volk, Marks & Company, Devon-Strafford Company, C. Pat Riley, Robert E. Plank, Griest Realty Company, Media Real Estate Company, Lori Incorporated, J.J. Gumburg Company, Washington Plaza, Inc., Penndale Towers, Inc., Saniel-Elkind Real Estate Co., Spiro Realty Company, Talenfeld Real Estate Co., John C. Clark Company, Yeo & Lukens Company, G.S. Rockey Company, and P.O. Naly Company.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections sustained. Praecipe for default dismissed. Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, landlords and sellers of form leases, filed preliminary objections in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania against an action brought by plaintiff attorney general that sought to enjoin defendants from actions allegedly in violation of the Pennsylvania Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law, 73 P.S. § 201-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff attorney general filed an action pursuant to the Pennsylvania Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law (Law), 73 P.S. § 201-1 et seq., to enjoin defendants, landlords and sellers of form leases, from using or selling leases containing certain clauses plaintiff believed to be illegal under Pennsylvania law and failed to inform lessees of certain rights under Pennsylvania's landlord and tenant statutes. Numerous defendants filed preliminary objections. The court sustained defendants' objections, dismissed plaintiff's praecipe for default against one defendant who failed to answer the complaint, and dismissed the complaint. The court held that leases of real property did not come within the purview of the Law. The court also held that plaintiff failed to identify any provisions in the leases that were illegal as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objections of defendants, landlords and sellers of form leases, dismissed plaintiff attorney general's praecipe for default, and dismissed plaintiff's complaint. The court held that the leasing of real property did not come within the purview of Pennsylvania's consumer protection laws and that the complaint failed to identify any provisions in the form leases that were per se illegal.

Hetherington v. McHale


Nos. 555 C.D. 1973, 559 C.D. 1973, 560 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


10 Pa. Commw. 501; 311 A.2d 162; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 565


June 4, 1973, Argued  
November 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in cases of Burton Hetherington, Earl Strite, G. W. Robinson, Duane Hartsell, T. A. Doebler and Jay Coble v. James A. McHale, Individually and as Secretary of Agriculture of the Commonwealtth of Pennsylvania, Bernard Hammer, Individually and as Acting Executive Secretary of the Pennsylvania Harness Racing Commission, Henry Nixon, Individually and as Director of Plant Industry, Thomas L. Rowland, Individually and as Director of Planning, Research and Governmental Services, and Raymond J. Kerstetter, Individually and as Deputy Secretary of Agriculture of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Nos. 555 and 559 C.D. 1973, and Burton Hetherington, Earl Strite, G. W. Robinson, Duane Hartsell, T. A. Doebler, and Jay Coble v. James A. McHale, Individually and as Secretary of Agriculture of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Robert P. Casey, as Auditor General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Grace M. Sloan, as Treasurer of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, No. 560 C.D. 1973.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff committee members, brought action in equity, quo warranto, and mandamus, seeking to enjoin meetings of or action by a committee unless plaintiffs participated therein. Plaintiffs sought, a declaration that they were proper members of the committee and should be seated thereon; to enjoin approval of any research project and allocation or expenditure of any funds for any projects unless plaintiffs participated in the committee action.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to statute, plaintiff committee members, were appointed to a committee empowered to make recommendations to defendant Secretary of Agriculture for the expenditure of funds for agricultural research projects. The attorney general declared portions of the statute unconstitutional and directed defendant secretary of agriculture not to seat plaintiffs. Plaintiffs suit sought to enjoin meetings of or action by the committee unless plaintiffs participated therein; sought judicial determination that plaintiffs were proper members of the committee and entitled to be seated thereon and sought to enjoin the approval of any research project and the allocation or expenditure of any funds for such projects unless plaintiffs participated in the committee action. The court held that the statute was constitutional and not an improper delegation of authority; did not usurp the governor's power of appointment; and was not special legislation. Further, the attorney general was without power or authority to declare a statute unconstitutional, and to implement his opinion so as to effectively abrogate or suspend any such statute.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the preliminary objections filed by defendants, state officials, in an action brought by plaintiffs, committee members, seeking to enjoin meetings of or action by the committee unless plaintiffs participated. The court held that the attorney general was without authority to declare portions of the statute to be unconstitutional and to direct defendant agriculture secretary, not to seat plaintiffs.

 

782 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania Power & Light Co. v. Pennsylvania Public Utility Com.


No. 398 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


10 Pa. Commw. 328; 311 A.2d 151; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 538


June 4, 1973, Argued  
October 12, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission in case of Petition of Pennsylvania Power & Light Company, Order of March 28, 1972 at Docket No. C. 19244.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility company sought review of the order of respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission which disallowed appellant's proposed utility rate increases.


OVERVIEW: Appellant utility company sought judicial review of the decision of respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission which disallowed appellant's proposed utility rate increases based upon a determination of "annual depreciation" of appellant's assets. On appeal, the court affirmed respondent's adjudication and dismissed appellant's challenge. The court held that there was no abuse of discretion by respondent in adopting the reserve requirement study. The court held that respondent was consistent in applying the same reserve requirement study methods and statistics for both accrued and annual depreciation. The court reasoned that the burden was upon appellant to prove that deficiency in its book reserves was "genuine" and that appellant had failed to prove that during the period of time in which the deficiency was developed that it did not receive sufficient revenue to pay all of its operating expenses plus a fair return on the fair value of its property devoted to the public service. Finally, the court held that respondent was within its discretionary authority to reject the remaining life theory proposed by appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication of respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, because respondent did not abuse its discretion by adopting the reserve requirement study and denying appellant utility company's proposed rate increase.

 

783 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Dussia v. Barger


No. 1099 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


10 Pa. Commw. 167; 309 A.2d 607; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 507


September 14, 1973, Argued  
September 26, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of Lieutenant Colonel Joseph Dussia v. Colonel James D. Barger, Commissioner of the Pennsylvania State Police, and Major Sidney C. Deyo, Captain Earl O. Bergstrom and Captain Stanley B. Kramer, members of the Court-Martial Board.



DISPOSITION: Motion refused.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings in his equity action against defendants, his employer the Commissioner of the State Police and other members of the Court-Martial Board (Pennsylvania), in which plaintiff sought to enjoin the conduct of his court-martial.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee brought a complaint in equity against defendants, his employer the Commissioner of the State Police and other Court-Martial Board members, in a suit to enjoin the conduct of his court-martial for alleged lack of due process. The court found no abuse of plaintiff's rights to due process because it did not appear that defendant employer inspired the charges against plaintiff or participated in the hearing of the charges, defendant employer's function on review was limited to nonarbitrary action founded on the record, and plaintiff had the right to an appeal. Plaintiff's motion for judgment on the pleadings was denied by the court because defendant employer's answer had raised unresolved issues of fact, and a motion for judgment on the pleadings could be granted only in a case free from doubt when no meritorious defense had been raised in the pleadings.


OUTCOME: Due to unresolved issues of fact, the court refused plaintiff employee's motion for judgment on the pleadings in his suit against defendants, his employer the commissioner and other members of the Court-Martial Board, in which plaintiff sought to enjoin the conduct of his court-martial.

 

784 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Scranton v. Lynn


No. 345 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


10 Pa. Commw. 222; 310 A.2d 451; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 516


February 5, 1973, Argued  
September 26, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, in case of Leo Lynn v. City of Scranton, No. 2063 September Term, 1971.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), declaring 53 P.S. § 101, which authorized city governing bodies to determine their own municipal classifications, was an unlawful delegation of legislative power in violation of Pa. Const. art. III § 20.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff appellee filed a petition for a declaratory judgment to have 53 P.S. § 101, which established city classifications and permitted cities to determine by ordinance which classification to adopt, declared unconstitutional as an unlawful delegation of legislative power. The court below granted the petition, and appellant city sought review. The court reversed. The statute in issue did not unlawfully delegate the legislative power to determine city classifications under Pa. Const. art. III, § 20. The legislature exercised this power in establishing the framework of classifications in the statute, and it was not an unconstitutional delegation to permit city legislative bodies to decide which of those classifications would be operative for a particular city. The classification, which relied upon population levels, was not special and local legislation even though only three cities within the state fell into the designated range at the time of enactment. The statute's application was not limited to those cities, because any city's population had the potential to increase or decrease to bring that city within the designated classifications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court order finding a statute unconstitutional which permitted cities, by ordinance, to determine their municipal classifications, because the statute did not unconstitutionally delegate the legislative power itself, but merely permitted the city to select a classification within a framework established by the legislature.

 

785 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Schubach v. Silver


No. 30 Tr. Dkt. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


9 Pa. Commw. 152; 305 A.2d 896; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 601


February 7, 1973, Argued  
June 8, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of Fred Schubach and Florence Schubach, Raymond Hrubovak and Doris Hrubovak, Dr. Leon S. Caplan and Rosemaire E. Caplan, and Alexander G. Allison and Dorothy M. Allison v. David Silver, Pine Hill Home, Inc., trading as Pine Hill Rehabilitation Center, Yellin and Co., City of Philadelphia and Girard Trust Bank, Intervening Defendant, No. 325 December Term, 1970. Transferred from the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania to the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, August 14, 1972.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owners of property neighboring appellee nursing home, challenged the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which held the city's rezoning of appellee's property to be valid. The rezoning followed a decision of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania that held that an earlier attempt to rezone a smaller area was invalid as spot zoning.


OVERVIEW: Appellee nursing home sought rezoning of its property to commercial. The city eventually granted rezoning by ordinance, but that ordinance was held to be invalid as spot zoning. The city passed another ordinance, which again rezoned appellee's tract, but included more property than the acres covered by the earlier ordinance. The trial court held that the second ordinance to be valid. Appellant neighboring property owners appealed. The court, at the outset, held that it was vested with jurisdiction even though appellants did not seek first to appeal to the zoning board of adjustment. The court held that, while the doctrine of res judicata was not dispositive of the appeal, collateral estoppel prevented the relitigation of various determinations. The court held that the second ordinance was not invalid on the basis of the purpose for which it was enacted, and that appellee either a present or an anticipated nuisance. The court found no basis for awarding punitive damages, but held that the second ordinance was invalid as spot zoning, because the ordinance thrust a commercially zoned peninsula into a residential sea without any apparent necessity for so radical a change.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that the ordinance in question did constitute spot zoning and was consequently invalid. The court held that res judicata did not apply, but that collateral estoppel applied to a number of factual findings in the previous decision. The court held that the challenged ordinance was not invalid on the basis of the purpose for which it was enacted. The court found no basis for punitive damages.

Hegedic v. DOT

CASE SUMMARY:

Frantz v. Baldwin-Whitehall School Dist.


No. 779 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


8 Pa. Commw. 639; 304 A.2d 531; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 777; 5 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1085; 7 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P9064


March 5, 1973, Argued  
May 9, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in case of Albert Frantz v. Baldwin-Whitehall School District, No. 2529 October Term, 1971.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of appellee school district, in appellant's action in mandamus for reinstatement and back pay claiming wrongful termination under 24 P.S. § 11-1122.


OVERVIEW: Appellant teacher was terminated by appellee school district, pursuant to 24 P.S. § 11-1122, when he was 62 years of age. Appellant filed an action in mandamus for reinstatement and back pay. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court stated that it was the clear intention of the legislature that a board of school directors could terminate the service of any professional employee who had attained the age of 62 and was not a member of the Social Security System pursuant to state statute, that appellant was such an employee, and that appellant's termination was in accord with the provisions of § 11-1122. The court concluded that appellant had not met the heavy burden of showing that appellee abused its discretion in terminating his services, and that while appellant was the only employee of his class whose services were terminated, neither that fact in itself nor the record established purposeful and intentional discrimination in violation of the equal protection guarantee of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of appellee school district, in appellant teacher's action in mandamus seeking reinstatement and back pay for wrongful termination, because appellee had acted within its discretion under the plain terms of the applicable statute, and appellant had not shown that he had been deprived of equal protection.

Gaebel v. Thornbury Township

8 Pa. Commw. 399; 303 A.2d 57; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 731

April 6, 1973, Decided

Property of William F. Gaebel and Virginia F. Gaebel, his wife, No. 2876 of 1972.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which sustained preliminary objections filed by appellee township in case regarding a zoning regulation.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that sustained the preliminary objections filed by appellee township because it found that appellant property owner's proper remedy to challenge the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance was under the review provisions of the Municipalities Planning Code, 53 P.S. § 10605. The court found that after the reclassification of a portion of appellant's land, they had petitioned for appointment of viewers for the value of loss damages to be ascertained under the Eminent Domain Code, 26 P.S. § 1-502(a). The court concluded that appellant's exclusive recourse was to challenge the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance under the provisions of review established by the Municipalities Planning Code, and that they could not avail themselves to the compensation provisions of the Eminent Domain Code. The court held that if the zoning ordinance was found to be constitutional as a reasonable regulation under the exercise of appellee's police power, then appellants would be entitled to monetary compensation and could have availed themselves to the Eminent Domain Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court order that sustained the preliminary objections of appellee township because it found that appellant property owners were required to challenge the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance under the Municipalities Planning Code before an utilization of the award determination provisions of the Eminent Domain Code.

Simco Stores, Inc. v. Redevelopment Authority of Philadelphia

Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County in case of A Condemnation Proceeding In Rem by Redevelopment Authority of the City of Philadelphia, for the purpose of Redevelopment of Center City Redevelopment Area, Market Street, East Urban Renewal Area, Section B, Designated as NDP Area IV, Philadelphia, Including Certain Land, Improvements and Properties, No. 3965 May Term, 1970.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners and tenants of commercial properties sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellants preliminary objections to appellee Redevelopment Authority of the City of Philadelphia's declaration of taking.


OVERVIEW: Appellee redevelopment authority condemned the commercial properties of appellant owners and tenants. Appellants filed preliminary objections to appellee's declaration of taking. Appellants' objections were dismissed and appellants sought review. The court affirmed the lower court's order. The court held that appellants' evidence fell far short of showing that none of the conditions leading to blight existed. The court held that the power of discretion over what areas are to be considered blighted is solely within the power of appellee. The court stated that it is presumed that the planning commission performed its duties in good faith. The burden was upon appellants to prove the contrary. The court found no evidence that the planning commission acted in a capricious or fraudulent manner or that its actions were based upon private motives. The planning commission's certification as to blight in the redevelopment area was made after extensive survey as to the existing land use, obsolete streets and walkways, and archaic traffic patterns.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that dismissed appellant owners and tenants' preliminary objections to appellee redevelopment authority's declaration of taking. The court found no evidence that the planning commission acted in a capricious or fraudulent manner or that its actions were based upon private motives.

Commonwealth v. National Gettysburg Battlefield Tower, Inc.


Nos. 120 C.D. 1972, 753 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


8 Pa. Commw. 231; 302 A.2d 886; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 710; 3 ELR 20347


December 6, 1972, Argued  
April 3, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania by the Honorable Milton J. Shapp, Governor, and the Honorable J. Shane Creamer, Attorney General and as Trustee for the People of the Commonwealth v. National Gettysburg Battlefield Tower, Inc., Thomas R. Ottenstein, Leroy E. Smith, Apple County Lodge, Inc., Jack Maitland and Hans Enggren, George A. Moose and Elizabeth Moose, trading and doing business as Stonehenge Motel and Restaurant, No. 2 July Term, 1971.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County (Pennsylvania), which concluded that appellant had not met its burden of proving that an observation tower proposed to be constructed by appellee landowners on the site of the battle of Gettysburg would so injure the values protected by Pa. Const. art. I, § 27, as to justify an order restraining erection of the tower.


OVERVIEW: Appellee landowners proposed building an observation tower on the Gettysburg battlefield, on private land not subject to federal regulation. Appellant commonwealth sought to restrain erection of the tower based on Pa. Const. art. I, § 27, which imposed a public trust on appellant to maintain and conserve the state's natural resources on the people's behalf. The lower court denied relief, holding that appellant had not established by clear and convincing evidence that the tower would injure constitutionally protected values to such a degree as to warrant the extraordinary injunctive relief sought. Appellees had agreed to locate the tower at a site acceptable to the National Park Service for the purpose of minimizing its adverse impact. The lower court made detailed findings concerning the tower, the commercial neighborhood, the agreement, and an ultimate finding that the tower would not injure natural, scenic, historic, or esthetic values but would provide educational benefit to those who used the park. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that appellant had not borne its burden of proof, and finding no clear error in the chancellor's fact findings and legal conclusions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which found that appellant commonwealth failed to meet its burden of proving by clear and convincing proof that the injunctive relief it sought was warranted. Applying the narrow standard of appellate review to the chancellor's findings and conclusions, the court found no clear error justifying reversal.

Marston v. Kline


No. 155 C.D. 1973


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


8 Pa. Commw. 143; 301 A.2d 393; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 697


February 23, 1973, Argued  
March 8, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of David W. Marston, Carmen Quanti, and Robert Becker, on their own behalf and on behalf of all others similarly situated v. Ernest P. Kline, Lieutenant Governor of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and C. Delores Tucker, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and Francis B. Patterson and Louis Menna and Eugene E. J. Maier, individually and as members of the County Board of Elections of Philadelphia County.



DISPOSITION: Complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individuals and members of the class of qualified electors, filed an original action in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), against defendants, lieutenant governor, commonwealth secretary, and members of the county board of elections, seeking that a special election be enjoined on grounds that the redrawn district resulted in a dilution of votes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, individuals and members of the class of qualified electors, filed an original action to enjoin a special election called to fill a vacancy for the remainder of the term of a deceased senator when that senatorial district no longer existed because of redistricting. Defendants, lieutenant governor, commonwealth secretary and members of the county board of elections, joined with plaintiffs in requesting that the court decide, as a matter of law, whether a special election should be held in the new second senatorial district as reconstituted after a proper reapportionment, in a hybrid senatorial district described by plaintiffs, in the old second senatorial district from which the deceased senator was elected, or at all. The court found that plaintiffs failed to show how the redistricting diluted their vote, and held that the special election must be held in the new senatorial district because the newly created district was the constitutional, legal, valid and proper district for all future elections, and that the writ of election was properly issued for the new senatorial district. The court dismissed plaintiffs' complaint.


OUTCOME: The complaint filed by plaintiffs, individuals and members of the class of qualified electors, seeking to enjoin the special election scheduled by defendants, lieutenant governor, commonwealth secretary and members of the county board of elections, was dismissed because the election was properly scheduled to take place in the new senatorial district as redistricted.

8 Pa. Commw. 118; 301 A.2d 93; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 695


January 8, 1973, Argued  
March 7, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original jurisdiction in case of David Oas, James Julian and Alice Fulgenzio, individually and on behalf of all citizens of the Girard School District and the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and on behalf of all school children of the Girard School District and the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Pennsylvania Department of Education, Pennsylvania State Tax Equalization Board, State Treasurer Grace Sloan, Girard School District and Edward J. Potter.



DISPOSITION: Motions to strike and objections to nonjoinder of necessary parties sustained. Complaint dismissed without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed suit against defendants, Commonwealth of Pennsylvania Department of Education, Pennsylvania State Tax Equalization Bond, State Treasurer, School Board, and local tax collector, challenging the imposition and collection of property taxes for educational purposes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers, faced with a recent increase in property taxes for school purposes, challenged the constitutionality of the method of financing public school education through taxation by respondent school board and commonwealth. The court dismissed plaintiff's claim for failure to join necessary parties. The court found that the school districts of Pittsburgh and Philadelphia should have been joined because plaintiffs claimed that these districts unconstitutionally received special aid, and any outcome of that claim would have directly affected them. The court granted respondents' motion to strike because the complaint asserted to be a class action, but plaintiffs did not allege that parties they contended to represent suffered the same or similar harms. Plaintiffs improperly described the class as including everyone in Pennsylvania. The complaint did not set forth any allegations as to how the assessment and levy of local property taxes were controlled by defendants, commonwealth, Pennsylvania Department of Education, Pennsylvania State Tax Equalization Bond, and State Treasurer. The case was dismissed without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed, without prejudice, plaintiff taxpayer's complaint that challenged the assessment and levy of local property taxes for school purposes. The court found that plaintiffs had not correctly identified a class for class action purposes, had failed to join necessary parties, and had not alleged how the tax assessment was controlled by defendant commonwealth.

Commonwealth v. Robinson


No. 525 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


7 Pa. Commw. 521; 300 A.2d 913; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 824

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas at Delaware County (Pennsylvania), upholding a suspension of appellant's operator's license for refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test as provided in the so-called "Implied Consent Law," 75 P.S. § 624.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant motorist was apprehended by a police officer for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, a violation of 75 P.S. § 1037, and, after being so charged, refused to submit to a breathalyzer test as provided in the so-called "Implied Consent Law," 75 P.S. § 624.1(a). Appellant's operator's license was suspended for six months. The trial court upheld the suspension, finding that the arrest for the stated violation was proper and that appellant was requested and refused to take a chemical test of his breath. The court affirmed. The court held that the evidence provided reasonable grounds for the officer to believe that appellant had been driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and that trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the arrest was lawful. The court held that the officer was not required to advise appellant that a refusal to take the breathalyzer test could result in the suspension of his license or that alternative tests were available.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, upholding a suspension of appellant motorist's operator's license for refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test. The court held that competent evidence supported the trial court's findings that the arrest for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor was lawful and that appellant was requested and refused to take a chemical test of his breath.
