Williams v. State Civil Service Com.


No. 322 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


7 Pa. Commw. 554; 300 A.2d 799; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 830


September 12, 1972, Argued  
February 23, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Civil Service Commission in case of In Appeal of Scott A. Williams, No. 1221.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the order of appellee State Civil Service Commission (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's challenge of his removal as an appeals referee by the appointing authority, who appellant claimed terminated him for non-merit factors in violation of 71 P. S. § 741.905(a) of the Civil Service Act, 71 P.S. § 741.1, et seq., and for his inability to qualify for veterans points under 51 P. S. § 492.3.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney had been appointed to a position of appeals referee, with provisional status, by the appointing authority. Later, that same authority appointed a second attorney to another appeals referee position. Appellee Civil Service Commission then conducted a civil service examination of both attorneys and used the results in determining that the second attorney was to receive a promotion. With that information, the appointing authority then terminated appellant, and he challenged this decision to appellee. He claimed that his termination was politically motivated, but appellee dismissed his claim. Appellant then challenged the determination, claiming that his employment was terminated for non-merit factors in violation of the Civil Service Act, 71 P.S. § 741.1, et seq., and that his inability to qualify for veterans' preference under the 51 P. S. § 492.3 violated his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because appellee claimed it as the basis for his termination. The court found no error committed by appellee and that appellant did not overcome the presumption of constitutional validity of 51 P. S. § 492.3, and therefore appellee's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of appellee State Civil Service Commission against appellant attorney's challenge of his removal from his position of appeals referee. Appellant had not shown that he did not receive the appointment for non-merit reasons and he did not meet his heavy burden of proving that his appointment was denied by virtue of any faulty classification under the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.

 

798 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Humphreys v. State Civil Service Com.


No. 454 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


7 Pa. Commw. 566; 301 A.2d 400; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 831


September 8, 1972, Argued  
February 23, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the State Civil Service Commission in case of Appeal of David J. Humphreys, No. 1236.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant civil servant challenged the order of appellee State Civil Service Commission, which terminated appellant from his position as an appeals referee because he lived outside of the district where he served and other qualified persons were promoted over him.


OVERVIEW: Appellant civil servant challenged the order of appellee State Civil Service Commission that terminated him from his position as an appeals referee. The court affirmed the order of appellee. The court found that appellant had not sustained his heavy burden of showing that the promotions statute was unconstitutional. There was a presumption that the legislation was constitutional. Under 4 Pa. Code 95.7(b)(3) only regular or probationary employees already within the classified service were considered for such promotions. Appellant's name was on the list but he was not already in the classified service. Additionally, the court found that 71 P. S. § 741.501 granted appellee the discretion to establish a requirement that appointees be residents of the district where the appointment was to be. Appellant stated he did not live in that district.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of appellee State Civil Service Commission that terminated appellant civil servant from his position as an appeals referee. The court found that the promotions statute employed by appellees was constitutional and appellant had failed to prove that it was not. Appellee was entitled to make a requirement that appointees live in the district they to which they were appointed.

 

799 of 1321 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Kready


No. 264 C.D. 1972


Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania


7 Pa. Commw. 448; 300 A.2d 291; 1973 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 819


September 13, 1972, Argued  
February 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, in case of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. B. Frank Kready, Jr., a/k/a Frank Kready, No. 42 Trust Book, page 135.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Suspension order reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which directed appellant to revoke the suspension of appellee driver's motor vehicle privileges. Appellant challenged the lower court's denial of its motion to quash, and its finding that appellant's action was unconstitutional under § 1413 of the Vehicle Code, 75 P.S. § 1413.


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver had his motor vehicle privileges suspended twice by appellant, the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation Appellee's challenge through a petition for special allowance of supersedeas, which the trial court recognized as an appeal of the suspension, was allowed on the ground that § 1413 of the Vehicle Code, 75 P.S. § 1413, was unconstitutional. Appellant alleged that § 1413 was constitutional and that the lower court erred in not granting its motion to quash. The court reversed the lower court's order. The court held that appellee had the right to take seek review of appellant's action, but his right was limited by the 30-day time period in § 620 of the Vehicle Code, 75 P.S. § 620. Although § 1413 did not specifically provide for an appeal, § 620 provided that remedy to appellant through Pa. Const. art. V, § 9, which granted a right of appeal to all citizens from an adjudication of an administrative agency. Appellee's challenge of his license suspension was untimely filed. Therefore, the court ordered the reinstatement of the suspension of appellee's motion vehicle privileges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order denying appellant, the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation's, motion to quash appellee driver's claim that his motor vehicle license be reinstated. The court held that the Vehicle Code was constitutional because appellee had the right to challenge it under the Administrative Agency Law. However, appellee's challenge of appellant's action was untimely filed; license suspension was reinstated.
